2:25:1501:0:14:72:325:700:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Information Acquisition in Rumor Based Bank Runs
2:26:1549:14:14:72:209:686:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Zhiguo He and Asaf Manela
2:27:1574:14:14:72:234:672:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:NBER Working Paper No. 18513
2:28:1602:14:14:72:246:658:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:November 2012, Revised June 2014
2:29:1634:14:28:72:182:644:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:JEL No. E61,G01,G21
2:30:1653:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:31:1661:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:We study information acquisition and dynamic withdrawal decisions when a spreading rumor exposes
2:32:1757:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:a solvent bank to a run. Uncertainty about the bank’s liquidity and potential failure motivates depositors
2:33:1863:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:who hear the rumor to acquire additional noisy signals. Depositors with less informative signals may
2:34:1963:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:wait before gradually running on the bank, leading to an endogenous aggregate withdrawal speed and
2:35:2061:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:bank survival time. Private information acquisition about liquidity can subject solvent-but-illiquid
2:36:2161:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:banks to runs, and shorten the survival time of failing banks. Public provision of solvency information
2:37:2264:14:42:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:can mitigate runs by indirectly crowding-out individual depositors’ effort to acquire liquidity information.
2:38:2372:42:14:72:124:462:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Zhiguo He
2:39:2381:14:14:72:179:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:University of Chicago
2:40:2402:14:14:72:196:434:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Booth School of Business
2:41:2426:14:14:72:205:420:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:5807 S. Woodlawn Avenue
2:42:2449:14:14:72:162:406:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Chicago, IL 60637
2:43:2466:14:14:72:124:392:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:and NBER
2:44:2474:14:28:72:215:378:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:zhiguo.he@chicagobooth.edu
2:45:2500:28:14:72:134:350:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Asaf Manela
2:46:2511:14:14:72:161:336:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Campus Box 1133
2:47:2526:14:14:72:175:322:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:One Brookings Drive
2:48:2545:14:14:72:174:308:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:St. Louis, MO 63130
2:49:2564:14:0:72:169:294:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:amanela@wustl.edu
3:50:2581:0:33:72:185:709:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:1  Introduction
3:51:2596:33:22:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Bank runs are unfortunately still with us. Runs occurred recently on major traditional banks such
3:52:2693:22:22:72:539:654:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:as Northern Rock and IndyMac, and on non-traditional “shadow” banks. In Section2, we document
3:53:2786:22:22:72:540:632:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:several intriguing features of the largest ever bank failure, which resulted from the 2008 run on
3:54:2883:22:22:72:540:610:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Washington Mutual: (i) the bank survived a first run, followed by deposit inflows; (ii) rumors circu-
3:55:2984:22:22:72:540:588:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:lated, but there was no public information of the first run happening; (iii) uncertainty about bank
3:56:3083:22:22:72:540:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:liquidity played a key role in a second fatal run; (iv) both runs had an important time dimension;
3:57:3181:22:22:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(v) worried depositors (even those covered by FDIC insurance) acquired additional information,
3:58:3275:22:22:72:540:522:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:then some withdrew immediately, while others decided to wait. The empirical pattern that runs
3:59:3368:22:21:72:540:500:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:have an important time dimension and that uncertainty and learning play a key role, has been
3:60:3460:21:22:72:540:479:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:documented as far back as the 1857 run on the Emigrant Industrial Savings Bank, and is especially
3:61:3557:22:22:72:540:457:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:important for the uninsured shadow banking system (e.g., money market funds behavior amid the
3:62:3650:22:22:72:539:435:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:European debt crisis discussed in Section2). The dynamic effects of information acquisition and
3:63:3745:22:22:72:540:413:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the incentives to wait, on the existence and duration of bank runs, have not been studied by existing
3:64:3846:22:22:72:270:391:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank run models. We aim to fill this gap.
3:65:3887:22:22:88:539:369:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We study dynamic rumor-based bank runs with endogenous information acquisition. Our model
3:66:3976:22:22:72:539:347:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:incorporates uncertainty about bank liquidity into the asynchronous awareness framework ofAbreu
3:67:4071:22:22:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and Brunnermeier(2003). A liquidity event occurs at some unobservable random time, at which
3:68:4162:22:22:72:540:303:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:point a solvent bank becomes illiquid with a known probability or remains liquid. An illiquid bank
3:69:4260:22:22:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:has only a limited amount of cash exposing it to a run, while a liquid bank has sufficient reserves to
3:70:4362:22:22:72:540:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:avoid a run. In the 07/08 financial crisis, the liquidity event can be thought of as banks with opaque
3:71:4464:22:22:72:540:237:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:exposure to mortgage-backed securities becoming weak and thus “illiquid” following adverse shocks
3:72:4561:22:21:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in the housing market. The liquidity event triggers the spread of arumorsaying the liquidity event
3:73:4659:21:22:72:540:194:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:has occurred and the bank may be illiquid, exposing the bank to a run. Agents (depositors) can
3:74:4753:22:22:72:540:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdraw or deposit funds back at any time for a small transaction cost, but in the unique bank
3:75:4848:22:22:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:run equilibrium, upon hearing the rumor, agents wait, fully withdraw, and then redeposit if the
3:76:4943:22:22:72:540:128:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank survives. The optimal withdrawal time trades-off the marginal benefit of waiting inside the
3:77:5039:22:22:72:540:106:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank due to the yield on deposits, with the marginal cost of waiting due to risk of loss in a bank
3:78:5137:22:0:72:105:84:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:failure.
4:79:5146:0:22:88:539:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We first show that a straightforward application ofAbreu and Brunnermeier(2003) to bank
4:80:5233:22:22:71:540:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:runswithoutinformation acquisition is rather uninteresting: in equilibrium,eitherbank runs never
4:81:5329:22:22:71:540:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:occur,ordepositors run on the bank immediately upon hearing the rumor.  Intuitively, if the
4:82:5420:22:22:71:539:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:conjectured (off-equilibrium) bank survival time is so long that every agent decides to wait a bit
4:83:5518:22:22:71:539:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:longer, then the illiquid bank would fail later. This longer survival time pushes agents to wait even
4:84:5619:22:22:71:539:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:longer. This force is so strong that, in equilibrium, agents never withdraw and the bank survives
4:85:5716:22:22:71:539:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:indefinitely, i.e. runs never occur. On the other hand, if every agent decides to withdraw a bit
4:86:5812:22:22:71:539:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:earlier, then the equilibrium force of a shorter bank survival time pushes all agents to withdraw
4:87:5909:22:22:71:539:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:immediately upon hearing the rumor. In this bank run equilibrium, the withdrawal speed and the
4:88:6003:22:22:71:488:511:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:implied bank survival time are exogenously determined by the rumor spreading speed.1
4:89:6087:22:22:88:539:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We then allow uncertainty-motivated informed agents who hear the rumor to acquire additional
4:90:6179:22:22:71:539:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:noisy signals. Our main result shows that private information acquisition about liquidity exposes
4:91:6276:22:21:71:539:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:otherwise safe banks to destructive runs with endogenous waiting. There are three potential signal
4:92:6374:21:22:71:540:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:realizations:good,fair, andbad, which are independent across agents conditional on the bank liquid-
4:93:6473:22:22:71:539:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ity state. Information acquisition with noisy signals creates belief heterogeneity among depositors,
4:94:6573:22:22:71:539:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:which is key to our result. A good or bad signal reveals the liquidity state perfectly. Receiving
4:95:6670:22:22:71:539:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a fair signal can be interpreted as seeing mixed evidences, leaving the agent still uncertain about
4:96:6769:22:22:71:539:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank liquidity as his prior. A higher quality signal is more likely to reveal the state perfectly. If the
4:97:6874:22:22:71:539:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank is indeed illiquid, then in aggregate a higher quality implies more agents receive bad signals
4:98:6973:22:22:71:231:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:thus knowing the bank is illiquid.
4:99:7007:22:22:88:539:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Fixing the signal quality, we show that in a setting where bank runs never exist otherwise, an
4:100:7101:22:22:71:539:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:interesting bank run equilibrium with endogenous waiting emerges once we allow agents to acquire
4:101:7197:22:22:71:539:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:information. Conditional on the bank being illiquid, agents with bad signals perceive a high bank
4:102:7294:22:22:71:539:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:failure hazard rate and withdraw immediately.  Agents with uninformative fair signals maintain
4:103:7388:22:22:71:539:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the same beliefs they had before acquiring the signals, but now also worry about withdrawals by
4:104:7483:22:21:71:539:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bad-signal agents—hence fair-signal agents withdraw earlier than they would otherwise. This effect
4:105:7581:21:22:71:539:139:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:goes a long way in changing the qualitative nature of the bank run equilibrium. In equilibrium,
4:106:7676:22:16:71:539:117:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:instead of waiting indefinitely, agents with fair signals wait some endogenous time, earning a yield on
4:107:7779:16:15:84:539:101:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:1In deriving the endogenous bubble burst time,Abreu and Brunnermeierresolve this issue by assuming that the
4:108:7886:15:11:72:540:86:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:bubble component increases over time. This would be a hard assumption to swallow in a bank run setting: it would
4:109:7998:11:0:72:427:75:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:require that for aperfectly liquid bankthe value of a dollar deposited declines over time.
5:110:8089:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:deposits, but withdraw once the failure hazard rate becomes substantial, leading to an endogenous
5:111:8186:22:22:72:267:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:equilibrium (illiquid) bank survival time.
5:112:8228:22:22:88:539:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The mechanism is as follows. Without information acquisition, all agents effectively have fair
5:113:8322:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:signals. If all agents were to wait longer, the equilibrium bank failure time would be delayed by
5:114:8419:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the same amount.  This force pushes all agents to wait indefinitely and thus banks never fail.
5:115:8513:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:With information acquisition, there is belief heterogeneity among depositors; specifically, there are
5:116:8614:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:both fair-signal and bad-signal agents conditional on the bank being illiquid. When all fair-signal
5:117:8713:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents wait a bit longer, the delay in bank failure is limited, because more bad-signal agents have
5:118:8812:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdrawn. A “fear-of-bad-signal-agents” increases the equilibrium hazard rate perceived by fair-
5:119:8909:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:signal agents, and results in a unique endogenous withdrawal time that equates the marginal cost
5:120:9005:22:22:72:180:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and benefit of waiting.
5:121:9028:22:22:88:539:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We then study the endogenous choice of signal quality with the bank run equilibrium. With
5:122:9117:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:this additional ingredient, our model features both strategiccomplementarityandsubstitutability
5:123:9212:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in information acquisition among individual agents.  Potential bank failure motivates agents to
5:124:9307:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:acquire higher quality signals, which in turn, shorten the equilibrium survival time of the failing
5:125:9406:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank. This positive spiral between bank runs and information acquisition makes bank runs more
5:126:9499:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:likely. We show that in an economy that without information acquisition is free of bank runs, there
5:127:9598:22:22:72:539:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:could be two equilibria once information acquisition is allowed: ano-run-no-acquisition equilibrium
5:128:9697:22:22:72:539:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:where agents do not acquire additional signals and do not run, and arun-acquisition equilibrium
5:129:9792:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:where agents acquire information aggressively and run on the illiquid bank.  Socially inefficient
5:130:9889:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:information acquisition about bank illiquidity thus exhibits strategic complementarity regarding
5:131:9985:22:22:72:226:248:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:whether to acquire information.2
5:132:10017:22:22:88:539:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:However, in our setting with smooth information acquisition costs, information acquisition
5:133:10107:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:exhibits strategic substitutability regardinghow much information to acquiredue to a learning
5:134:10200:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:effect. In our model there is a natural “public” signal conveyed by the fact that the bank has not
5:135:10298:22:21:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:yet failed. If others study more about the bank and run on the illiquid one, then the illiquid bank
5:136:10397:21:16:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:fails faster. As a result, this public signal becomes more informative. Because a more informative
5:137:10495:16:15:84:540:123:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:2This positive feedback effect is similar toHellwig and Veldkamp(2009) who show that in their particular static
5:138:10606:15:11:71:539:108:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:setting, information acquisition exhibits complementarity if and only if ensuing actions (in our model, running on
5:139:10720:11:11:71:539:97:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:the bank) are complementary.  In other economic settings, information acquisition complementarity arises even
5:140:10829:11:11:71:539:86:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:though ensuing actions are not complementary; one such example is the ex ante investment in high-frequency trading
5:141:10943:11:0:71:311:75:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:technology analyzed inBiais, Foucault, and Moinas(2013).
6:142:11000:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:public signal lowers the value of private signals, individual agents hearing the rumor respond by
6:143:11097:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:acquiring less information.  This learning effect also explains a counter-intuitive result that the
6:144:11196:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:wider the awareness window over which the rumor spreads, implyingmorepotential withdrawers,
6:145:11287:22:22:72:539:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:thelongerthe illiquid bank survives. The intuition is that conditional on the bank surviving thus
6:146:11384:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:far, the bank is more likely to be liquid given that the rumor could have started spreading a long
6:147:11482:22:22:72:369:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:time ago, which discourages incentives to acquire information.
6:148:11544:22:22:88:539:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We extend our model along two dimensions. First, we consider fundamentally insolvent banks.
6:149:11635:22:22:72:539:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:When agents privately collect information about banksolvency, they inevitably learn about bank
6:150:11729:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:liquidity. Effort spent acquiring one reduces the effort needed to acquire the other. We show that
6:151:11827:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:public provision of solvency information curbs the private acquisition of bank liquidity information
6:152:11927:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and delays a bank’s failure, which, even for a short while, can help both regulators and industry
6:153:12024:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:organize an orderly resolution that minimizes damage to the banking system.3Thus our model
6:154:12114:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:implies that carefully constructed stress tests can help prevent or mitigate bank runs by crowding
6:155:12212:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:out information acquisition by individuals.  Second, we show it is beneficial to avoid providing
6:156:12308:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:too much information that differentiates competing solvent but potentially illiquid banks, as small
6:157:12407:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:differences in liquidity can result in runs on slightly weaker banks. This justifies U.S. government
6:158:12507:22:22:72:482:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:actions that forced all “Big 9” banks to take government capital on October 13, 2008.
6:159:12592:22:22:88:540:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Our model is related to a vast literature on the role of information instaticbank runs, and
6:160:12683:22:22:72:539:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:it is beyond the scope of our paper to have a thorough review on this topic.4The distinguishing
6:161:12778:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:feature is gradual withdrawal, which is an important aspect of modern bank runs (see Section2).
6:162:12873:22:22:71:539:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The dynamic nature of bank runs has been explored by studying the sequential service constraint
6:163:12968:22:22:71:540:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in theDiamond and Dybvigsetting.Green and Lin(2003) point out that no bank runs exist if
6:164:13056:22:22:71:539:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:depositors know their clock times of arrival and thus infer their relative positions in the queue,
6:165:13154:22:16:71:539:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:whilePeck and Shell(2003) show that bank runs exist if the relative queue position information is
6:166:13251:16:11:84:466:188:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:3See March 16, 2008,Financial Timesarticle titled “Bear races to forge deal with JPMorgan.”
6:167:13342:11:15:84:540:177:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:4See Gorton (1985),Bhattacharya and Gale(1987),Jacklin and Bhattacharya(1988),Chari and Jagannathan
6:168:13441:15:11:71:539:162:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:(1988), and recently,Ennis and Keister(2009). Our model provides an information-based theory of bank panics as
6:169:13551:11:11:71:540:151:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:opposed to a sunspot-based theory (Gorton and Winton,2003, Ch. IV). On the topic of information acquisition and
6:170:13662:11:11:71:540:140:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:bank runs,Nikitin and Smith(2008) study how information acquisition about banksolvencyaffects the bank run
6:171:13768:11:11:71:539:129:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:equilibrium in a staticDiamond and Dybvigsetting. In contrast, we focus on information acquisition about bank
6:172:13877:11:11:71:540:118:9:g_d0_f9:9:g_d0_f8:liquidity. Based on theMorris and Shin(2002) global games technique,Goldstein and Pauzner(2005) study the
6:173:13982:11:11:71:539:107:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:optimal deposit contract by deriving a unique equilibrium when depositors in aDiamond and Dybvigtype setting
6:174:14090:11:11:71:539:96:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:are endowed with private noisy signals about bank fundamentals. We allow for endogenous information acquisition,
6:175:14202:11:0:71:538:85:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:and show that excessive socially wasteful learning may lead to socially inefficient runs on solvent-but-illiquid banks.
7:176:14322:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:unavailable.5In this regard, our paper is similar toPeck and Shell(2003) since each agent in our
7:177:14418:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:model assigns the same distribution to her relative position in the queue. Relative to these models,
7:178:14518:22:22:72:500:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:we emphasize the endogenous interaction between information acquisition and bank runs.
7:179:14604:22:22:88:539:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Gu (2011) studies depositors’ withdrawal strategy sequentially for a potentially insolvent bank in
7:180:14702:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a Diamond and Dybvigsetting. Unlike our paper, (some) depositors inGu (2011) observe previous
7:181:14795:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdrawals. Because withdrawals indicate bank insolvency,Gu (2011) shows that herding (ignoring
7:182:14891:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:private information which is endowed exogenously) after a long sequence of withdrawals may lead
7:183:14986:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to inefficient bank runs. Our paper with endogenous information quality emphasizes individual
7:184:15079:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:depositors’ uncertainty and forming of rational expectation over other depositors’ withdrawal timing
7:185:15179:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and strategies.  This aspect is important given the modern age of electronic banking, the high
7:186:15273:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:frequency nature of repo in the context of shadow banking, or the large scale runs by money market
7:187:15371:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:funds that faced the European sovereign debt crisis. Thus our mechanism is complementary toGu
7:188:15464:22:21:72:500:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(2011) in understanding the dynamics of bank runs together with the role of information.
7:189:15552:21:22:88:539:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:From a modeling perspective, our framework features more empirically appealing timing as-
7:190:15641:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:sumptions in that individual depositors can withdraw or redeposit their funds at any time; this
7:191:15736:22:22:72:539:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:represents a substantial improvement from theDiamond and Dybvigframework and the above-
7:192:15823:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:mentioned important extensions. If high frequency micro-level data is available, our analytically
7:193:15920:22:22:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tractable model is particularly calibration-friendly thanks to its empirically-interpretable time di-
7:194:16021:22:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:mension.6An alternative approach to bank run modeling isHe and Xiong(2012a,b) who develop
7:195:16110:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:dynamic debt run models of a firm with a time-varying fundamental and a staggered debt structure.
7:196:16207:22:22:88:540:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Rumors are studied byBanerjee(1993) andvan Bommel(2003). We build on the approach
7:197:16288:22:22:72:539:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of Abreu and Brunnermeier(2002,2003) who consider the asynchronous timing of awareness to
7:198:16377:22:22:72:539:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:study “rational” bubbles.7We add to their model uncertainty about the capacity of the bubble
7:199:16469:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(bank), decouple the spreading rate from the length of the awareness window, and allow agents
7:200:16562:22:16:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to acquire additional noisy information upon awareness. This ex post heterogeneity generates the
7:201:16658:16:14:84:539:166:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:5This literature focuses on optimal mechanism design; for related papers, seeWallace(1988,1990),Andolfatto,
7:202:16765:14:7:72:319:152:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:Nosal, and Wallace(2007), andAndolfatto and Nosal(2008).
7:203:16821:7:15:84:540:145:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:6By contrast,Green and Lin(2003) andPeck and Shell(2003) study finite-agent economy, and depositors can
7:204:16924:15:11:72:540:130:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:either withdraw at period 1, when called in line, or wait until period 2.Gu (2011) considers a relaxation that a finite
7:205:17043:11:11:72:540:119:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:number of depositors can withdraw at any time within an interim stage before period 2. A significant departure
7:206:17153:11:11:72:540:108:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:from theDiamond and Dybvigframework seems necessary for developing dynamic models that are both calibration-
7:207:17261:11:11:72:540:97:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:friendly and tractable. A sacrifice our model makes is to assume away the preference (early or late) type of depositors,
7:208:17381:11:7:72:381:86:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:an ingredient critical forDiamond and Dybvig, but inessential for our paper.
7:209:17457:7:0:84:536:79:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:7Brunnermeier and Morgan(2010) generalize this idea to a class of “clock games” and test its main predictions.
8:210:17568:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:fear-of-bad-signal-agent effect, which naturally leads fair-signal agents to withdraw earlier, giving
8:211:17669:22:22:72:480:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rise to a bank run equilibrium in which the illiquid bank fails at an endogenous time.
8:212:17755:22:22:88:540:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The paper proceeds as follows. Section2 summarizes empirical facts on bank run dynamics.
8:213:17843:22:22:71:540:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Section3 builds a rumor-based bank run setting. Section4 shows that information acquisition
8:214:17934:22:22:71:539:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:with noisy signals leads to an interesting bank run equilibrium with an endogenous (aggregate)
8:215:18028:22:22:71:539:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdrawal speed.  Section5 discusses empirical predictions of our model.  Section6 provides
8:216:18120:22:45:72:462:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:extensions and discussion. We conclude in Section7. Proofs are in the Appendix.
8:217:18199:45:33:71:309:532:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2  Empirical Bank Run Evidence
8:218:18229:33:22:71:539:499:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We begin by providing new evidence about the failure of Washington Mutual (WaMu), and syn-
8:219:18319:22:22:71:539:477:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:thesizing the empirical literature on bank run dynamics. Many of the stylized facts about runs on
8:220:18416:22:22:71:539:455:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:traditional regulated commercial banks also appear in shadow bank runs. In organizing these facts
8:221:18513:22:22:71:539:433:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:about bank runs, we highlight three aspects that are key contributions of our model: (i) bank runs
8:222:18611:22:22:71:539:411:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are dynamic and gradual with rumors spreading among depositor-like agents; (ii) uncertainty and
8:223:18706:22:22:71:539:389:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:learning about the bank’s liquidity drive agents’ withdrawal/redeposit behavior; and (iii) individual
8:224:18807:22:38:71:395:367:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents are actively acquiring their own information before they run.
8:225:18875:38:29:71:207:329:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.1  Traditional Banks
8:226:18897:29:21:71:539:300:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Figure1 shows that the runs on WaMu were dynamic in nature. The bank suffered two separate
8:227:18987:21:22:71:539:279:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:runs: it experienced gradual withdrawals of $9 billion during a first run lasting 20 days in July
8:228:19084:22:22:71:539:257:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:2008, and withdrawals of $15 billion during a second run lasting 15 days in September 2008, leading
8:229:19183:22:22:71:223:235:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:up to its takeover by the FDIC.
8:230:19214:22:22:88:539:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Information and uncertainty play an important role in both runs on WaMu.  Following the
8:231:19301:22:22:71:539:191:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:failure of IndyMac on July 11, 2008, WaMu experienced massive withdrawals but managed to
8:232:19389:22:22:71:539:169:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:survive. Interestingly, consistent with our modeling of “rumor” as “information without discernible
8:233:19488:22:22:71:539:147:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:origin” in Section3.1.3, although plenty of rumors about it circulated online, this run was never
8:234:19585:22:16:71:540:125:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:publicly reported before WaMu’s failure.8After this first run, the bank regained much of its deposit
8:235:19685:16:15:84:539:109:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:8Some examples from answers.yahoo.com dated July 26, 2008: (1) “Anybody else hear rumors about WaMu bank
8:236:19789:15:11:72:540:94:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:potentially being taken over by the Federal Government? I heard that it is failing too. Who’s next? Is it time to
8:237:19902:11:11:72:540:83:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:make that run yet?” (2) “I heard the same thing...I have a Wamu bank card....Yaaaaaaaaaaahooooooo! This means
8:238:20011:11:0:72:540:72:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:I can tap it out and the Government will bail me out.” (3) “I am so glad I took my money out.” (4) “Actually I heard

9:253:20758:33:22:72:540:391:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:base, suggesting that the mere survival of WaMu conveys positive information to its depositors. In
9:254:20856:22:22:72:540:369:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:September 2008 after Lehman Brothers failed, uncertainty regarding WaMu’s liquidity and hence
9:255:20949:22:22:72:540:347:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:its eventual fate played a key role in a fatal second run. The bank’s ability to secure funds from

9:257:21143:22:20:72:539:303:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:some depositors withdrew while others decided to wait.10Such noisy information acquisition and
9:258:21237:20:7:72:532:283:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:they had did better than expected in earnings. Only rumor I heard was that National City was going to be next.”
9:259:21348:7:15:84:539:276:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:9WaMu depended on borrowings from the FHLBs of San Francisco and Seattle and the San Francisco Fed acting as
9:260:21456:15:11:72:540:261:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:lenders of last resort. Given its composite CAMELS rating of 4, there was no assurance that funds would be available
9:261:21572:11:10:72:540:250:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:in the amounts and in the timing needed to meet its obligations. In fact, the bank lost its access to the Term Auction
9:262:21690:10:11:72:540:240:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:Facility program. See September 25, 2008 letter by Darrel W. Dochow, OTS Regional Director recommending FDIC
9:263:21798:11:8:72:122:229:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:receivership.
9:264:21811:8:14:80:539:221:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:10“All across the country, customers streamed into hundreds of WaMu branches, on edge, brimming with questions.
9:265:21922:14:11:72:540:207:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:This run was nothing like July’s, which had been tame by comparison. Now people were frenzied, acting purely out
9:266:22034:11:11:72:540:196:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:of fear. ‘We just didn’t have any control,’ said one branch manager. The tellers’ talking points no longer placated the
9:267:22153:11:11:72:540:185:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:customers—even the tellers didn’t understand them. ‘They kept telling us to say that we have $44 billion, whatever
9:268:22267:11:11:72:540:174:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:that meant,’ said one employee, likely referencing WaMu’s liquidity position. The customers demanded to talk to
9:269:22378:11:11:72:540:163:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:whoever was in charge. At one Seattle location, they lined up and waited all day to speak to the branch manager.
9:270:22490:11:11:72:540:152:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:‘Should I take my money out?’ they asked her when they reached her, over and over again. ‘Is WaMu going under?’
9:271:22601:11:11:72:540:141:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:And they asked the inevitable question: ‘What wouldyoudo?’ The branch manager, who knew most of the people’s
9:272:22709:11:11:72:540:130:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:names and their kids, would say, ‘I don’t know any more than you do. But if you’re uncomfortable, do what makes
9:273:22820:11:11:72:540:119:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:you sleep at night.’ She wasn’t sleeping, either. ‘You went to work and you go hammered,’ the branch manager said
9:274:22933:11:11:72:540:108:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:later. ‘By the end of the day, you were exhausted. And you didn’t know if you had a job, or what was going on.’
9:275:23044:11:11:72:540:97:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:WaMu headquarters told the branches repeatedly that everything was fine, but the news reports and the blogs and
9:276:23155:11:11:72:540:86:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:the stories posted on Facebook all said otherwise. ‘You told the customers something, and then they watched the
9:277:23266:11:0:72:540:75:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:news, and then they would come back,’ the branch manager said. Many took their money out anyway.” (Grind,
10:278:23372:0:22:72:397:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the decision to wait before running are the main focus of our paper.
10:279:23440:22:22:88:539:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Surprisingly, more than half of running WaMu depositors were in fact covered by FDIC insur-
10:280:23531:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ance. Withdrawals by insured depositors could make sense if they worry the FDIC might tem-
10:281:23621:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:porarily freeze their accounts, or that it could not afford to cover WaMu’s insured deposits which
10:282:23719:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:were several times the Deposit Insurance Fund at the time, or simply as one depositor explained,
10:283:23815:22:22:72:254:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:they “just don’t want to deal with it.”
10:284:23854:22:22:88:539:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Iyer and Puri (2012) document the dynamic nature of an Indian bank run influenced by its
10:285:23942:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:depositors’ social network.  They also find that deposit insurance is only partially effective in
10:286:24039:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:preventing runs. Unlike in WaMu’s first run in July 2008, deposit balances of most depositors who
10:287:24136:22:22:72:349:511:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:ran on the Indian bank, did not return to pre-run levels.11
10:288:24195:22:22:88:539:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:O Grada and White(2003) find that the 1857 bank run on the Emigrant Industrial Savings Bank
10:289:24286:22:22:71:540:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:had an important time dimension: “In neither 1854 nor 1857 did depositors respond to a single
10:290:24379:22:21:71:539:445:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:signal that led them to crowd into banks all at once. Instead, panics lasted a few weeks, building
10:291:24477:21:22:71:540:424:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:and sometimes ebbing in intensity, and only a fraction of all accounts were closed.” They conclude
10:292:24575:22:22:71:539:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that the 1857 run was driven by informational shocks in the face of asymmetric information about
10:293:24671:22:22:71:540:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the true condition of bank portfolios.Kelly and O Grada(2000) provides further evidence on
10:294:24761:22:38:71:269:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:information transmission during this run.
10:295:24802:38:29:71:187:320:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2.2  Shadow Banks
10:296:24819:29:22:71:539:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Maturity transformation is no longer exclusively done in traditional commercial banks. Shadow
10:297:24912:22:22:71:539:269:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:banks, which include securitization vehicles and investment banks, provides short-term funding for
10:298:25010:22:22:71:539:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:long-term projects in a broad sense and has developed into an unregulated substitute to traditional
10:299:25109:22:22:71:539:225:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:commercial banks. With short-term funding contracts akin to demand deposits, these “shadow”
10:300:25200:22:22:71:305:203:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:banks are subject to runs with similar features.12
10:301:25250:22:19:88:539:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In September 2008 the Securities and Exchange Commission conducted an audit of the collapse
10:302:25341:19:11:72:539:162:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:2012, p. 277-278). See also July 24, 2008,Bloombergarticle titled “WaMu Slumps as Gimme Credit Cites Liquidity
10:303:25451:11:7:72:111:151:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:Concern.”
10:304:25460:7:15:80:539:144:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:11In our main model with a single bank (which can be either liquid or illiquid), depositors return to the surviving
10:305:25575:15:11:72:540:129:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:bank once they endogenously learn it is liquid. In Section6.2 we introduce competing banks. There, withdrawing
10:306:25685:11:7:72:539:118:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:depositors never return to their original bank, which offers a possible rationale for the findings ofIyer and Puri(2012).
10:307:25806:7:15:80:539:111:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:12For instance,Gorton and Metrick(2011),Covitz, Liang, and Suarez(forthcoming), andAcharya, Schnabl, and
10:308:25910:15:11:72:540:96:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:Suarez(2013) document “shadow” bank runs on repo and asset-backed commercial paper (ABCP).Schroth, Suarez,
10:309:26016:11:0:72:478:85:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:and Taylor(2013) find that runs on ABCP are sensitive to leverage, asset values, and asset liquidity.
11:310:26118:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of Bear Stearns. Consistent with our modeling of dynamic nature of rumor, the executive sum-
11:311:26210:22:22:72:539:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:mary starts with: “During the week of March 10, 2008, rumors spread about liquidity problems at
11:312:26305:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:Bear Stearns. As the rumors spread, Bear Stearns was unable to obtain secured financing from
11:313:26397:22:22:72:155:643:11:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:counterparties.”13
11:314:26415:22:22:88:539:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Given the sophisticated multi-layered structure of the modern financial system, “bank runs”
11:315:26506:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:can be interpreted broadly as funding withdrawals by one class of short-term lenders (i.e., not just
11:316:26606:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:household depositors) from other institutions. For instance, during the 2011 European sovereign
11:317:26701:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:debt crisis, money market funds (like depositors) divested from European banks. Fears of liquidity,
11:318:26800:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:or rollover risk, rather than solvency drove fund managers to cut their exposure to Spanish and
11:319:26895:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Italian banks.14Consistent with our model, this run was dubbed the “slow-motion” bank run in
11:320:26987:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the popular press, referring to its gradual nature: money market funds reduced their exposure
11:321:27080:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to all Eurozone banks by 37% from $453 billion to $287 billion between May and August 2011
11:322:27170:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(Chernenko and Sunderam(2012)). More interestingly, individual information acquisition played a
11:323:27265:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:crucial role, as fund managers each did their own research and came up with different conclusions,
11:324:27363:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:prompting some to run and others to rollover their investment.15Eventually, U.S. money market
11:325:27456:22:22:72:539:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:funds returned to the European money market.16Their return to these positions is hard to generate
11:326:27553:22:46:71:404:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:using existing models, but is a feature of ours, which we turn to next.
11:327:27624:46:32:71:445:312:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3  The Base Model without Information Acquisition
11:328:27673:32:22:71:539:280:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We first build a rumor-based bank run model by introducing uncertainty into the asynchronous
11:329:27765:22:22:71:539:258:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:awareness setting ofAbreu and Brunnermeier(2003), which is our base setting without information
11:330:27860:22:22:71:539:236:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:acquisition. Most of the analysis here, such as learning and optimal withdrawal strategies, applies
11:331:27959:22:22:71:539:214:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to later situations with information acquisition. We show that, without information acquisition,
11:332:28055:22:22:71:540:192:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:eitherbank runs do not occur at all,ordepositors run on the bank immediately upon hearing the
11:333:28148:22:16:71:539:170:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rumor. Therefore, bank runs, if they occur, exhibit an exogenous withdrawal speed, which implies
11:334:28244:16:15:80:539:154:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:13“SEC’s oversight of Bear Stearns and related entities: The consolidated supervised entity program,” report no.
11:335:28356:15:11:72:540:139:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:446-A published on September 25, 2008. Interestingly, Chairman Christopher Cox described Bear Stearns as a well-
11:336:28468:11:11:72:539:128:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f9:capitalized entity, which “was done in by a cash shortage, because lending dried up and prime-brokerage clients moved
11:337:28585:11:11:72:540:117:9:g_d0_f9:9:g_d0_f8:their money elsewhere” (April 3, 2008, Bloomberg article titled “Cox Defends SEC’s Role in Regulating Bear Stearns
11:338:28699:11:7:72:124:106:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:(Update1)”).
11:339:28711:7:11:80:478:99:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:14See July 24, 2011,Financial Timesarticle titled “Money market funds cut euro bank exposure.”
11:340:28805:11:11:80:462:88:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:15See July 5, 2011,Reutersarticle titled “U.S. money funds diverge on European bank paper.”
11:341:28896:11:0:80:476:77:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:16See July 29, 2013,Financial Timesarticle titled “US money market funds return to EU banks.”
12:342:28990:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the bank fails at some exogenous time. This result changes qualitatively once we allow agents to
12:343:29086:22:38:72:261:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:acquire additional noisy private signals.
12:344:29127:38:29:72:172:649:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.1  The Setting
12:345:29143:29:29:72:226:620:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:3.1.1  Bank and Depositors
12:346:29169:29:22:72:540:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Time is continuous ont∈[0,∞).  There is a unit mass of infinitely-lived risk-neutral agents
12:347:29260:22:22:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(depositors) with a zero discount rate. Bank deposits yield a constant rate of returnr >0when the
12:348:29357:22:22:72:540:547:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank is operating, while holding cash outside the bank earns nothing. Broadly, one can interpret the
12:349:29457:22:22:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank as some investment vehicle in the shadow banking system or even the entire financial system,
12:350:29554:22:22:72:540:503:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and the positive relative wedge reflects either a higher investment growth rate or a convenience
12:351:29650:22:22:72:540:481:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:yield for keeping funds in the institution.  Our main analysis focuses on a single bank, but we
12:352:29745:22:22:72:456:459:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:consider competing banks offering similar returns as an extension in Section6.2.
12:353:29825:22:22:88:539:437:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:To avoid exploding values for a dollar inside the potentially safe bank, we assume that the
12:354:29916:22:21:71:540:415:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank’s growth stops at some “maturing” event modeled as a Poisson shock with intensityδ > r, and
12:355:30012:21:22:72:539:394:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:afterwards the game ends (e.g., each agent gets his deposit back for consumption).17Throughout,
12:356:30107:22:38:71:470:372:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:this maturing event is independent of any other random variables that we consider.
12:357:30189:38:29:71:297:334:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:3.1.2  Uncertainty about Bank Liquidity
12:358:30228:29:21:71:539:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:There are two potential types of banks that are fundamentally solvent (i.e., bank survival is the
12:359:30325:21:22:71:539:284:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:first-best allocation), with one type of bank being “illiquid,” and a second “liquid” bank impervious
12:360:30426:22:22:71:539:262:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to runs. Uncertainty about bank liquidity is crucial to our analysis, though its source could be
12:361:30522:22:22:71:176:240:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:fundamental shocks.18
12:362:30543:22:22:88:539:218:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Bank liquidity is defined as the mass of depositors it takes to run down the bank. For simplicity,
12:363:30641:22:22:71:539:196:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:we assume a binary structure for the state of bank liquidity ̃κ. When the bank is illiquid, ̃κtakes a
12:364:30742:22:22:72:540:174:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:lower valueκL<1, and it fails when aκLmeasure of depositors have fully withdrawn their funds.
12:365:30835:22:16:72:540:152:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:One can literally interpret ̃κas the bank’s cash reserves to meet withdrawals. We broadly interpret
12:366:30934:16:15:80:539:136:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:17A similar but more natural interpretion is that individual agent suffers liquidity shocks with immediate consump-
12:367:31049:15:11:72:540:121:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:tion need (therefore withdrawal). The analysis, which is available upon request, is similar but much more complicated
12:368:31166:11:7:72:214:110:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:(due to the replacement of agents).
12:369:31201:7:15:80:539:103:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:18We consider uncertainty with known probabilities (risk). Generalizing our model to Knightian uncertainty might
12:370:31313:15:0:72:207:88:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:be interesting for future research.
13:371:31350:0:22:72:539:709:10:g_d0_f17:11:g_d0_f4: ̃κas the liquidity of the bank, which could represent uncertainty about the willingness of a lender
13:372:31450:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of last resort (e.g. central bank) to lend to bank (see footnote9 for an example). For the liquid
13:373:31547:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank with a higher liquidity reserve, ̃κ=κH> κL. We focus on the case that there is no run on
13:374:31640:22:22:72:539:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the liquid bank; hence for now it is useful to think ofκH>1, i.e. the sufficiently liquid bank can
13:375:31738:22:22:72:539:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:survive any severe run. However, in Section6.3.1we verify that our asynchronous awareness model
13:376:31833:22:22:72:353:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:can haveκH<1but still rule out runs on the liquid bank.
13:377:31888:22:22:88:539:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In our economy, it is common knowledge that conditional on the liquidity event (to be introduced
13:378:31984:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shortly), the probability of the illiquid state isp∈(0,1).When the illiquid bank fails, its assets
13:379:32082:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:have a fire-sale price to recoverγ∈(0,1)dollar for each dollar of deposits. Afterwards, all agents
13:380:32180:22:22:72:306:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:go to autarky consuming their remaining wealth.
13:381:32227:22:22:88:539:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We focus on uncertainty about liquidity for solvent banks for better comparison to the litera-
13:382:32321:22:22:72:539:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ture.19Section2.2 documents that during the 2007/08 financial crisis, concerns regarding liquidity
13:383:32419:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of financial institutions are often highlighted among investors and regulators. No doubt, both sol-
13:384:32518:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:vency and liquidity are highly linked to bank fundamentals. In reality, banks are not just either
13:385:32615:22:22:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:solvent or insolvent; within solvent banks, there are strong ones and weak ones that differ in their
13:386:32715:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:fundamentals. Our modeling of liquid/illiquid banks can be equivalently interpreted as strong/weak
13:387:32813:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:banks. Indeed, as detailed in the next subsection, one can interpret the illiquid bank as an institu-
13:388:32914:22:22:72:540:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tion whose capital base is hit by adverse shocks to its mortgage-backed securities, making it weak
13:389:33012:22:37:72:539:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:but still solvent. Later in Section6.1 we introduce fundamentally insolvent banks as an extension.
13:390:33110:37:29:72:430:277:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:3.1.3  Liquidity Event, Spreading Rumors, and Informed Agents
13:391:33171:29:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Att= 0the bank is liquid, i.e., ̃κ=κH. At some unobservable random time ̃t0>0referred to
13:392:33259:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:as the liquidity event, the bank may become illiquid, and the uncertainty is as modeled in Section
13:393:33357:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:3.1.2. Mapping to the 2007/08 crisis in which banks have opaque exposure to real estate, one may
13:394:33453:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:think of this event as the gradual deterioration of mortgage-backed securities which hurts banks’
13:395:33550:22:22:72:539:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:liquidity but keeps them solvent. Although the exact liquidity event timet0is publiclyunobservable,
13:396:33649:22:22:72:540:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:it is common knowledge that ̃t0is exponentially distributed on[0,∞)with cumulative distribution
13:397:33744:22:22:72:307:116:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f4:Φ (t0)≡1−e−θt0, whereθis a positive constant.
13:398:33789:22:16:88:540:94:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Knowledge of this liquidity event starts spreading in the population after ̃t0, i.e., some agents
13:399:33886:16:0:80:455:78:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:19For instance,Nikitin and Smith(2008) andGu (2011) focus on bank solvency information.
14:400:33975:0:22:72:539:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:hear a “rumor” that “the liquidity event ̃t0has occurred and thus the bank might be illiquid.”
14:401:34069:22:22:71:540:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Since the exact liquidity event time ̃t0is unknown, this spreading information captures the essence
14:402:34168:22:22:71:539:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of an unverified rumor of uncertain origin that spreads gradually in the depositor population.
14:403:34262:22:22:71:540:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Importantly, hearing the rumor informs the agent that “the liquidity event ̃t0has occurred and
14:404:34356:22:22:72:385:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:hence other agents in the population may have heard the rumor.”
14:405:34419:22:22:88:539:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We call those agents who hear the rumor “informed,” or simply “agents,” and the rest “unin-
14:406:34510:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:formed.” Since att= 0the bank is liquid, throughout we assume that agents’ beliefs are such that
14:407:34606:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:they stay inside the bank unless they hear the rumor. In Section6.3.2we show this is indeed the
14:408:34701:22:22:72:457:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:case under certain conditions, by analyzing the problem of an uninformed agent.
14:409:34780:22:22:88:539:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Given a realization of ̃t0=t0, the rumor begins to spread over an interval[t0,t0+η]with a
14:410:34869:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:positive constant (exogenous) lengthη. FollowingAbreu and Brunnermeier(2003) we refer toηas
14:411:34960:22:22:72:539:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the “awareness window.” At any interval[t,t+dt]wheret∈(t0,t0+η), uninformed agents become
14:412:35049:22:21:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:informed by hearing this rumor with probabilityβdt, whereβis an exogenous positive constant.
14:413:35141:21:22:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The rumor shock is i.i.d. across the population of uninformed agents. Then fort∈[t0,t0+η], the
14:414:35235:22:22:72:539:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:mass of uninformed and informed agents aree−β(t−t0)and1−e−β(t−t0)respectively, and the mass
14:415:35326:22:22:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of newly informed agents within[t,t+dt]isβe−β(t−t0)dt. To make the problem interesting, we
14:416:35416:22:22:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:assume that at timet0+ηthe fraction of informed agents, which is1−e−βη, is sufficient to take
14:417:35509:22:22:72:277:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:down the illiquid bank, i.e.,1−e−βη> κL.
14:418:35549:22:22:88:540:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This spreading technology is different from that ofAbreu and Brunnermeier(2003) in that we
14:419:35639:22:22:72:539:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:allow for separation between the spreading rateβand the awareness windowη.20As shown later,
14:420:35730:22:22:72:435:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the awareness windowηhas interesting effects opposite to common wisdom.
14:421:35801:22:22:88:540:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Call the informed agent who hears the rumor atti≥t0simply agentti.  Consistent with
14:422:35884:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:electronic age banking, he neither observes withdrawals before him, nor the potential queue in
14:423:35978:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:front of the bank.  In the context of shadow banking, given the high frequency nature of repo
14:424:36071:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:financing, we assume that individual creditors do not observe, but do form rational expectations
14:425:36167:22:21:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:about, other creditors’ rollover decisions.  We share withAbreu and Brunnermeier(2003) the
14:426:36257:21:22:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:simplifying assumption that agents do not observe the market price of bank equity, which future
14:427:36352:22:16:72:297:117:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:work can introduce by adding noise to prices.21
14:428:36399:16:7:80:403:101:6:g_d0_f7:6:g_d0_f21:20Abreu and Brunnermeier assume a linear spreading technology with rate1
14:429:36471:7:10:398:540:94:6:g_d0_f22:9:g_d0_f8:ηso that the entire population is
14:430:36504:10:8:72:462:84:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:informed att0+η. This way, the awareness windowηis artificially tied to the spreading rate1η.
14:431:36597:8:0:80:539:76:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:21If investors trading in the stock market have the same information as depositors, then bank stock prices convey
15:432:36712:0:29:72:329:709:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:3.1.4  Transaction Costs and Agent’s Problem
15:433:36756:29:22:72:540:680:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:To eliminate strategies with infinite transactions, we assume a constant, yet arbitrarily small,
15:434:36852:22:22:72:539:658:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:transaction costcper dollar when the agent receives cash from, or deposits cash back in the bank—
15:435:36949:22:22:72:539:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:including the maturing event (so the agent receives1−cper dollar of deposit) or bankruptcy (so
15:436:37043:22:22:72:532:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:he receivesγ(1−c)). This assumption is innocuous as our analysis carries through whenc→0.
15:437:37132:22:22:88:539:592:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In sum, after hearing the rumor an agent can withdraw his deposits whenever he believes bank
15:438:37224:22:22:72:540:570:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:failure is imminent, and redeposit this cash in the future if the bank’s survival sufficiently improves
15:439:37327:22:22:72:539:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:his posterior belief, both subject to a transaction costc. Due to the linearity of this problem, a
15:440:37425:22:22:72:510:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:“bang-bang” strategy, i.e. keeping the entire wealth either in or out of the bank, is optimal.
15:441:37519:22:22:88:539:504:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Our model allows for the possibility of depositors redepositing back to the bank, unlike exist-
15:442:37614:22:22:72:539:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ing literature based on theDiamond and Dybvigmodel (e.g.,Green and Lin(2003),Gu (2011),
15:443:37701:22:22:72:540:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:etc). Though it is not necessary for our qualitative results, the redepositing option is empirically
15:444:37801:22:21:72:539:438:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:motivated and theoretically appealing. Redepositing behavior is apparent in Figure1, which shows
15:445:37897:21:22:72:540:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that after the first run on WaMu, the bank regained much of its deposit base.  From a theory
15:446:37989:22:22:72:540:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:perspective, we find it more coherent to allow agents to deposit or withdraw at any time, with
15:447:38083:22:22:72:540:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:some transaction costs. We take up this challenge and show that before the bank fails the class of
15:448:38181:22:22:72:540:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:threshold strategies is optimal. Otherwise, the optimality of threshold strategies becomes trivial
15:449:38279:22:38:72:304:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:given an assumption that prohibits redepositing.
15:450:38327:38:29:72:154:291:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.2  Learning

20:649:47026:28:29:72:225:436:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.4  Bank Run Equilibria
20:650:47050:29:30:72:408:407:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We define a bank run equilibrium and a no run equilibrium as follows:
20:651:47119:30:22:72:540:377:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f4:Definition 1.Abank run equilibriumis a symmetric stationary Perfect Bayesian Nash equilibrium
20:652:47212:22:22:72:540:355:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in which informed agents’ strategies depend on the time since they heard the rumor, and the bank
20:653:47308:22:31:72:483:333:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:survival time is finite. Ano run equilibriumis when the bank survival time is infinite.
20:654:47395:31:22:88:539:302:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We focus on symmetric equilibria where ex ante identical agents take the same strategy. Sta-
20:655:47487:22:22:72:539:280:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tionarity here means that agentti’s strategy depends onτ=t−ti, nott; it follows from the
20:656:47575:22:22:72:539:258:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:hazard rate’s independence of the absolute timetiat which the agent becomes informed. A bank
20:657:47667:22:22:72:540:236:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:run means the illiquid bank fails at a finitet0+ζ <∞, while a no run equilibrium means the
20:658:47757:22:22:72:540:214:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank survives forever. Of course, a no run equilibrium always exists without further refinements
20:659:47853:22:22:72:540:192:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:on the behavior of agents, since ignoring the rumor is an equilibrium for solvent-but-illiquid banks.
20:660:47954:22:16:72:454:170:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Throughout, our focus is on the existence and properties of bank run equilibria.
20:661:48034:16:14:80:539:154:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:25We emphasize that the sufficient parameter condition12, which facilitates our analysis with detailed functional
20:662:48147:14:11:72:540:140:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:forms greatly, is far from the tight necessary condition. The optimality of threshold strategy is fairly general as long
20:663:48267:11:0:72:200:129:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:as the hazard rate is monotone.

22:709:50539:38:29:72:334:649:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:3.4.2  Characterizing the bank run equilibrium

22:727:51126:29:0:254:396:460:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f14:(1−p) (eλη−1) + (eλτr−1)p
22:728:51151:0:39:470:539:467:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:,(13)
22:729:51156:39:22:71:458:428:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:which captures the same individual optimality of withdrawal as in Proposition 2.
22:730:51236:22:22:88:539:406:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The aggregate withdrawal condition in (AW) determines the equilibrium remaining survival
22:731:51324:22:40:71:404:384:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:timeτur, where ‘u’ indicates upper bound as will shortly become clear
22:732:51393:40:0:260:295:344:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f15:τur≡−
22:733:51398:0:15:296:346:352:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f16:ln (1−κL)
22:734:51407:15:0:318:324:337:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f14:β
22:735:51408:0:39:348:539:344:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:.(14)
22:736:51413:39:22:72:539:305:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Once plugging this equilibriumτurinto (13), Proposition2 allows us to evaluate whether individual
22:737:51510:22:22:72:540:283:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents want to wait longer or withdraw earlier, depending on the sign ofG(τur). Recall that a
22:738:51603:22:22:71:539:261:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:lowerGis associated with a low marginal cost of staying (sayγclose to one). IfG(τur)<0, agents
22:739:51697:22:22:71:539:239:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:always want to wait, thus bank runs never occur. On the other hand, withdrawing earlier is optimal
22:740:51795:22:22:71:539:217:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:underG(τur)>0, implying immediate withdrawalsτw= 0in equilibrium, with an exogenous (or at
22:741:51885:22:22:71:540:195:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:most trivially endogenous) survival timeζ=τur=−ln(1−κL)β. Since the waiting time is cornered at
22:742:51980:22:22:72:539:173:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f18:zero, the equilibrium survival time mechanically depends only on the capacity of illiquid bankκL
22:743:52076:22:22:71:540:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and the rumor spreading speedβ. Finally, in a knife-edge case withG(τur) = 0, agents are totally
22:744:52172:22:31:71:456:129:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:indifferent, thus equilibria are indeterminate. We have the following proposition.
22:745:52254:31:22:71:493:98:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f5:Proposition 3.The bank run equilibrium without information acquisition is as follows:
22:746:52339:22:0:71:539:76:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:1. IfG(τur)>0, the unique bank run equilibrium is that every informed agent withdraws immedi-
23:747:52434:0:22:72:409:708:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:ately upon hearing the rumor, so thatτw= 0, andζ=τur=−ln(1−κL)β.
23:748:52498:22:22:72:334:686:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:2. IfG(τur)<0, a bank run equilibrium does not exist.
23:749:52551:22:22:71:539:664:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f16:3. If the primitive parameters are such thatG(τur) = 0, then in this knife-edge case, anyτw≥0
23:750:52644:22:30:71:314:642:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:andζ=τw+τurconstitute a bank run equilibrium.
23:751:52689:30:22:88:540:612:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Consider the second case in Proposition3. Hypothetically, imagine that each agent believes
23:752:52779:22:22:71:539:590:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:others are running immediately withτw=  0henceζ=τur.  BecauseG(τur)<0, each agent
23:753:52860:22:22:71:540:568:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:postpones withdrawal, say toτw= ∆>0.26But the aggregate withdrawal condition (AW) says
23:754:52946:22:22:71:540:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that the survival time adjusts one-to-one toζ=τur+∆. Then, given the new bank survival time, the
23:755:53042:22:22:71:539:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:individual optimality condition (IO) implies that the new waiting time responds one-to-one again
23:756:53138:22:22:71:540:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withτw= ∆ + ∆ = 2∆. Applying this thought experiment repeatedly implies that both waiting
23:757:53227:22:22:71:539:480:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:time and bank survival time are postponed indefinitely. Clearly, this logic reverses ifG(τur)>0,
23:758:53323:22:22:71:539:458:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:pushing agents to withdraw as early as possible—hence in equilibrium they withdraw upon hearing
23:759:53418:22:22:71:122:436:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the rumor.
23:760:53428:22:22:88:539:414:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The third knife-edge case is uninteresting, not only because of its indeterminacy of bank run
23:761:53521:22:22:71:539:392:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:equilibria but also because it holds only on a parameter space with zero measure. For the latter
23:762:53617:22:22:71:539:370:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:reason, the knife-edge case is not “generic,” and we only focus on generic equilibria throughout the
23:763:53717:22:45:71:154:348:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rest of the paper.
23:764:53735:45:33:71:383:303:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:4  The Model with Information Acquisition
23:765:53776:33:22:71:539:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In the base model above, the aggregate withdrawal condition (AW) implies that the survival time
23:766:53871:22:22:71:540:248:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:ζresponds one-to-one to changes in the waiting timeτw, and vice versa according to the individual
23:767:53968:22:21:71:539:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:optimality condition (IO). This somewhat interlocked stationarity is behind the tension between
23:768:54063:21:22:71:517:205:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:conditions (AW) and (IO) that precluded bank runs with waiting except in a knife-edge case.
23:769:54154:22:22:88:540:183:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In deriving the endogenous bubble burst time,Abreu and Brunnermeier(2003) resolves this
23:770:54241:22:22:71:539:161:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:issue by assuming that the bubble component of prices increases over time. As a result, the net
23:771:54336:22:22:71:539:139:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f18:benefit of attacking increases, so that in theindividual optimality conditionthe waiting timeτw
23:772:54431:22:22:71:540:117:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:responds less than one-to-one to the survival timeζ. In a bank run setting, this would be a hard
23:773:54527:22:16:71:539:95:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:assumption to swallow, which would require that the value of a dollar in a perfectly safe bank
23:774:54621:16:0:80:469:79:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:26Implicitly, it says thatG(τ∗r−∆) = 0which is the condition for the optimal withdrawal time.

24:784:54866:9:0:396:400:611:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f14:q
24:785:54870:0:8:384:398:656:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f15:1−
24:786:54872:8:0:399:403:648:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f14:q
24:787:54873:0:126:397:401:675:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f14:q
24:788:54874:126:22:72:221:549:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:declines exogenously over time.
24:789:54905:22:22:88:539:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In this paper we take a novel route.  We introduce noisy information acquisition, and thus
24:790:54995:22:22:72:539:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ex-postheterogeneityamong agents with different perceptions about the likelihood of bank failure.
24:791:55092:22:22:72:540:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:Different fromAbreu and Brunnermeier(2003), this naturally changes theaggregate withdrawal
24:792:55182:22:22:71:540:461:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f4:conditionso that the survival timeζresponds less than one-to-one to the waiting timeτw. As we
24:793:55275:22:22:71:539:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:show, this translates to a realistic “fear-of-bad-signal-agents” effect for those agents with median
24:794:55375:22:22:71:496:417:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:signal realizations, and a unique bank run equilibrium with endogenous waiting emerges.
24:795:55462:22:22:88:539:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We find that individual information acquisition regarding bank liquidity makes solvent banks
24:796:55554:22:22:71:539:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that are free from runs prone to runs, and shortens the survival time of failing banks. The point is
24:797:55654:22:22:71:539:351:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that, although bank runs never exist if information acquisition is not possible, inefficient bank runs
24:798:55756:22:21:71:539:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:with endogenous waiting reemerge once we allow for the possibility of acquiring additional signals,
24:799:55855:21:38:71:490:308:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:because individual information acquisition imposes negative externalities on each other.
24:800:55943:38:29:71:369:270:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:4.1  Information Acquisition and Signal Structure
24:801:55992:29:22:71:539:241:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:At timeti> t0when agentihears the rumor, he can acquire an additional signal about the bank’s
24:802:56085:22:22:71:539:219:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:type at some cost. For example, agents could spend time sifting through call reports, calling their
24:803:56184:22:22:71:539:197:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:branch manager, etc. To emphasize that it is the noisiness of the signal, rather than its precision,
24:804:56284:22:22:71:539:175:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that plays the crucial role, we first assume a binary information acquisition structure: either no
24:805:56382:22:22:71:539:153:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:acquisition, or acquiring an additional signal with a fixed precisionq >0. We endogenizeqin
24:806:56473:22:22:71:325:131:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Section4.4 by assuming a quadratic acquisition cost.
24:807:56525:22:22:88:539:109:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Agents payχ >0per dollar of deposits for the additional signal. Supposeχis realtively small
24:808:56616:22:0:71:539:87:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that when facing a bank run equilibrium it is optimal to acquire the signal. For tractability, the
25:809:56716:0:22:72:539:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:signal takes three possible values ̃y∈ {yL,yM,yH}with conditional probabilities as in Figure2.
25:810:56810:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:With probabilityq >0, the bank’s type is perfectly revealed by the signalyH(yL); while with
25:811:56901:22:22:72:539:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:probability1−q, the agent receives an uninformative “medium” signalyM(e.g., seeing mixed
25:812:56989:22:22:72:124:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:evidences).
25:813:57000:22:22:88:539:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Conditional on the bank’s state, the realizations of these signals are i.i.d. across agents. Uncon-
25:814:57099:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ditionally, the signals are correlated across agents, as signals tend to be low (high) in the illiquid
25:815:57201:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(liquid) state. Hence there are more agents with unfavorable signals given the bank being illiquid,
25:816:57300:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a feature captured by the simple signal structure in Figure2.27We emphasize that this signal
25:817:57392:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:structure is consistent with the fact documented in Section2.2, that during the Euro zone crisis,
25:818:57489:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:money market fund managers each did their own research and came up with different conclusions.
25:819:57583:22:22:88:540:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The analysis of optimal withdrawal strategies in Section3.3 applies once we condition on the
25:820:57675:22:22:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:signal realization. ForyH(yL) agents, we can simply replace the priorpwith0(1) in Proposition
25:821:57768:22:21:72:539:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:2. Agents withyHknow the bank is not subject to runs and thus stay inside the bank always. For
25:822:57862:21:40:72:341:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents withyL, it is optimal to withdraw immediately if
25:823:57917:40:0:208:271:384:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f16:g(0;p= 1) =

25:833:58380:14:14:80:540:185:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:27More formally, we need the signal to be informative on average, i.e.,Cov[ ̃y, ̃κ]>0. Our results are robust to the

28:997:64139:11:11:71:539:97:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:Then,τrthat solves the above equation will violateyMagents’ individual optimality condition (17) generically. As

28:999:64363:11:0:72:341:75:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:agents withdraw earlier which pushesζall the way to fall belowη.
29:1000:64429:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:immediately (τw= 0) so that the remaining survival timeτrtakes its upper boundτur(graphically,
29:1001:64523:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:settingτw=  0in the left panel of Figure3).G(τur)<0implies that the marginal cost of
29:1002:64607:22:22:72:539:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:waiting is outweighed by the marginal benefit, and eachyMagent postpones his withdrawal, say
29:1003:64699:22:22:72:143:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:toτw= ∆>0.
29:1004:64709:22:22:88:539:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:OnceyMagents decide to wait longer by∆>0, importantly they know there are moreyLagents
29:1005:64795:22:22:71:539:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdrawing before them—this is the key difference from the base model without signal acquisition
29:1006:64892:22:22:71:540:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:where all agents wait longer by∆. Bank failure now requires less withdrawingyMagents, and
29:1007:64981:22:22:71:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:hence a shorterτr< τurin (AW’). A shorter remaining survival timeτrimplies bank failure is more
29:1008:65076:22:22:71:539:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:imminent, giving rise to a higher failure hazard rate in (3) and a greater marginal cost of waiting.
29:1009:65176:22:22:71:539:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This captures the realistic “fear-of-bad-signal-agents” effect in the bank run environment: agents
29:1010:65274:22:22:71:539:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:unsure about bank liquidity (i.e.yMagents who receive mixed evidences) worry that there are
29:1011:65365:22:22:71:539:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents receiving much worse signals and thus running before them, which increases their incentives
29:1012:65463:22:21:71:539:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to run as well.31Finally, ifyMagents wait sufficiently long that the remaining survival time attains
29:1013:65563:21:0:71:225:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f14:its lower boundτr=τlr, thenG
29:1014:65591:0:11:226:232:435:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:(
29:1015:65592:11:0:232:241:424:11:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f18:τlr
29:1016:65595:0:11:241:247:435:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:)
29:1017:65596:11:22:251:540:424:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:>0implies that they want to withdraw a bit earlier. Then,
29:1018:65653:22:22:71:539:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:by the intermediate value theorem, a bank run equilibrium exists for some intermediateτrwith
29:1019:65745:22:22:71:540:380:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:G(τr) = 0, even though a bank run equilibrium does not exist if no acquisition of liquidity signals
29:1020:65844:22:37:71:120:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:is allowed.
29:1021:65855:37:29:71:486:321:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:4.3  Bank Run Equilibrium with Endogenous Information Acquisition
29:1022:65920:29:22:71:539:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We have derived the bank run equilibrium, given that every agent acquires the signal upon hearing
29:1023:66017:22:22:71:539:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the rumor. We now study the agent’s incentive to acquire the signal, given the bank run equilibrium.
29:1024:66117:22:22:71:539:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Recall Lemma2 states thatζ≤ηholds generically in any bank run equilibrium. As we will discuss
29:1025:66210:22:22:71:540:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in detail in Section4.5, this implies that hearing the rumor and observing the bank is still alive
29:1026:66308:22:22:71:539:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:attiis informative, and agentti’s posterior probability of the bank being illiquid, denoted bypti,
29:1027:66406:22:25:71:146:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:drops frompto
29:1028:66419:25:0:220:243:157:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f16:pti=

30:1081:68412:22:22:72:540:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The multiplicity of equilibria reflects the strategic complementarity of information acquisition com-

30:1086:68839:22:22:88:540:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Proposition5 supposesG(τur)<0. Suppose insteadG(τur)≥0, i.e., bank runs occur even
30:1087:68921:22:22:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:if agents cannot acquire liquidity information and they are already withdrawing upon hearing
30:1088:69013:22:22:72:540:137:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the rumor.  The next corollary shows that in equilibrium agents acquire information, then run
30:1089:69106:22:22:72:539:115:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:immediately on the illiquid bank that generates equal (yM) or worse (yL) signals only.  Hence

31:1093:69443:22:22:71:539:687:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:quisition. Then with information acquisition, in the unique bank run equilibrium agents acquire
31:1094:69538:22:31:71:537:665:11:g_d0_f5:11:g_d0_f5:information, withdraw immediately givenyMandyLsignals, and the illiquid bank fails atζ=τur.
31:1095:69629:31:22:88:539:634:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In general, collecting information about the bank’s liquidity status is individually beneficial
31:1096:69724:22:22:72:540:612:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:but socially wasteful, in the situation where without the additional information runs do not occur.
31:1097:69823:22:22:72:540:590:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:However, if without the additional information bank runs did occur, information acquisition could
31:1098:69920:22:22:72:540:568:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:mitigate runs on stronger banks.32Moreover, collecting information about bank solvency could be
31:1099:70015:22:22:72:315:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:socially beneficial, a topic we revisit in Section6.1.
31:1100:70069:22:22:88:539:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Belief heterogeneity is key to generating the interesting bank run equilibrium with endoge-
31:1101:70160:22:22:72:540:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:nous waiting, which feeds back to agents’ ex ante information choice.  Endogenous information
31:1102:70253:22:22:72:540:480:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:acquisition offers perhaps the most natural way to introduce belief heterogeneity into the model.
31:1103:70350:22:21:72:539:458:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Exogenously endowed noisy signals, i.e.χ= 0, would suffice to generate the bank run equilibrium

31:1106:70641:22:22:72:539:393:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Proposition5. A strictly positive signal cost eliminates such an uninteresting equilibrium, because
31:1107:70740:22:38:72:331:371:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents do not acquire signals that they plan to ignore.

33:1220:73652:117:13:72:539:424:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Panels (a) and (c) show the equilibrium survival time of the illiquid bankζ(solid line) and the waiting
