33:1222:73860:14:13:72:540:397:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:additional signalq, as a function of the rumor spreading rateβand the length of the awareness windowη.
33:1223:73962:13:45:71:540:384:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Parameters arer= 0.09,β= 1,θ= 1.03,η= 2,p= 0.8,δ= 0.12,c= 10−6,κL= 0.65,α= 0.7,γ= 0.75.
33:1224:74049:45:29:72:522:339:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:4.5  Strategic Complementarity vs. Substitution in Information Acquisition
33:1225:74123:29:22:72:539:310:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Our model features both strategiccomplementarityandsubstitutabilityin information acquisition
33:1226:74216:22:22:72:540:288:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:among individual agents. For better understating, we first take the model in Section4.4 and study
33:1227:74313:22:21:72:539:266:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the comparative statics of the rumor spreading rateβand the awareness windowη. Recall that
33:1228:74403:21:22:72:539:245:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:relative toAbreu and Brunnermeier(2003), our model decouples the rumor spreading rate from
33:1229:74493:22:22:72:180:223:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the awareness window.
33:1230:74514:22:22:88:539:201:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The comparison between these two comparative static results are intriguing. The top panels
33:1231:74604:22:22:72:539:179:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of Figure4 shows that, intuitively, the greater the rumor spreading rateβ, the faster the illiquid
33:1232:74702:22:22:72:540:157:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank fails (Panel4a), and the greater precision the acquired signals (Panel4b). A surprising result
33:1233:74801:22:22:72:540:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:emerges when we turn to the awareness windowηin the bottom panels. Whenηincreases so that
33:1234:74890:22:22:72:540:113:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:everybody knows that potentially there will be more informed agents attacking the bank, each
33:1235:74982:22:0:72:540:91:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:individual agent acquireslessinformation (Panel4d) and the illiquid bank surviveslonger(Panel
34:1236:75077:0:22:72:90:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:4c).
34:1237:75081:22:22:88:539:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Dynamic learning when faced with uncertainty plays a key role here. The posterior probability
34:1238:75174:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that the bank is illiquid upon hearing the rumor andobserving that the bank is still alive, recalling
34:1239:75275:22:40:72:217:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:thatΦ (t|ti)is given by (2), is:
34:1240:75307:40:0:94:118:603:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f16:pti=
34:1241:75311:0:14:148:328:610:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f15:Pr{bank survives atti|κL,ti}Pr{κL}
34:1242:75345:14:0:122:354:596:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f15:Pr{bank survives atti|κL,ti}Pr{κL}+ Pr{κH}
34:1243:75387:0:0:359:367:603:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f16:=
34:1244:75388:0:14:390:477:610:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f14:[1−Φ (ti−ζ|ti)]p
34:1245:75404:14:0:372:496:596:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f14:[1−Φ (ti−ζ|ti)]p+ 1−p
34:1246:75425:0:40:520:539:603:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(21)
34:1247:75429:40:39:72:453:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The posterior probability that the illiquid bank survives attiis decreasing inη:
34:1248:75509:39:0:90:387:524:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f15:Pr{illiquid bank survives atti|κL,ti}= 1−Φ (ti−ζ|ti) = 1−
34:1249:75566:0:15:391:465:531:11:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f19:eλη−eλ(ti−ti+ζ)
34:1250:75581:15:0:411:445:516:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f16:eλη−1
34:1251:75586:0:0:470:478:524:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f16:=
34:1252:75587:0:15:483:516:531:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f16:eλζ−1
34:1253:75592:15:0:483:516:516:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f16:eλη−1
34:1254:75597:0:40:518:521:524:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f14:.
34:1255:75598:40:22:72:539:484:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Intuitively, from the point of view of agentti, a greaterηimplies thatt0∈[ti−η,ti]could occur
34:1256:75691:22:22:72:540:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:earlier, and other depositors may have run on the bank for a longer time. As a result, conditional
34:1257:75789:22:22:72:386:440:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:on the bank being alive atti, the bank is more likely to be liquid.
34:1258:75856:22:22:88:539:418:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We have seen that in our bank run setting, information acquisition exhibits strategic comple-
34:1259:75949:22:21:72:539:396:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:mentarity regardingwhether to acquire information. This is evident from the existence of multiple
34:1260:76046:21:22:72:539:375:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:equilibria in Proposition5 with binary information choices: the information acquisition of other
34:1261:76142:22:22:72:540:353:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents makes a bank run possible, which prompts this agent to acquire his information as well. In
34:1262:76239:22:22:72:540:331:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:this way, acquisition of liquidity information can subject solvent but illiquid banks to runs. This
34:1263:76338:22:22:72:539:309:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:positive feedback effect shares the same spirit toHellwig and Veldkamp(2009) who show that, in
34:1264:76432:22:22:72:540:287:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a static model, information acquisition exhibits complementarity if actions (in our model, running
34:1265:76530:22:22:72:211:265:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:on bank) are complementary.
34:1266:76557:22:22:88:539:243:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In the setting with smooth information acquisition cost, (21) implies that individual information
34:1267:76654:22:22:72:540:221:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:acquisition exhibits strategic substitutability regardinghow much information to acquire. This is
34:1268:76751:22:22:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:because there is a natural public signal conveyed by the fact that the bank has not yet failed. If
34:1269:76849:22:22:72:540:177:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:others study more about the bank and run on the illiquid one, then the illiquid bank fails sooner.
34:1270:76947:22:22:72:540:155:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:As a result, this public signal becomes more informative—(21) suggests that the mere survival of
34:1271:77043:22:22:72:540:133:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the bank, upon hearing the rumor, leads the agent to perceive the bank to be stronger. Because
34:1272:77137:22:21:72:540:111:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a more informative public signal lowers the value of private signals, individual agents hearing the
34:1273:77236:21:15:72:509:90:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:rumor respond to the public signal of “bank survival tillti” by acquiring less information.34
34:1274:77329:15:0:80:539:75:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:34This is similar to the effect of price information in a noisy Rational Expectation Equilibrium (REE) asset pricing
35:1275:77447:0:22:88:539:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The result thatηmitigates bank runs goes against the casual intuition that runs are more
35:1276:77535:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:severe with more prone-to-run agents, which stems from the premise that bank failure requires a
35:1277:77630:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:sufficient mass of running depositors. By contrast, we show that in a dynamic learning setting,
35:1278:77725:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:when cumulative informed agents are enough to run down the bank, artificially shortening the
35:1279:77817:22:46:72:516:621:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:awareness window gives rise to a novel information effect with the exact opposite direction.35
35:1280:77911:46:32:72:249:575:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:5  Empirical Predictions
35:1281:77935:32:22:72:540:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Beyond the empirical bank run evidence presented in Section2, our model offers additional insights
35:1282:78033:22:22:72:502:521:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for future empirical research, especially for high-frequency deposits and withdrawals data.
35:1283:78124:22:22:88:539:499:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:First, our model makes several qualitative testable predictions about the nature of bank runs.
35:1284:78218:22:22:72:540:477:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Specifically, bank runs would empirically manifest as follows. There are two broad types of deposi-
35:1285:78317:22:22:72:540:455:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tors, with one type better informed than the other. These better informed agents start withdrawing
35:1286:78415:22:22:72:540:433:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:first, then joined by less informed agents. Importantly, a unique prediction of our model is that
35:1287:78512:22:22:72:540:411:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for banks that survive a run, we should observe some agents withdrawing at the same time other
35:1288:78606:22:22:72:540:389:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents are redepositing back into the bank. This cannot occur in a model where a homogeneous
35:1289:78698:22:22:72:451:367:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:depositor population responds to a common signal as inHe and Xiong(2012a).
35:1290:78772:22:22:88:539:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Second, our comparative statics generate testable predictions about how bank run dynamics
35:1291:78861:22:21:71:540:323:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:would respond to variation in key model parameters, such as those shown in Figure4.  Since
35:1292:78951:21:22:71:539:302:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rumors are often not made public, it could be challenging to empirically measure the endogenous
35:1293:79046:22:22:71:540:280:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdrawal time and bank survival time. However, the remaining survival timeτr, which is the
35:1294:79138:22:22:71:539:258:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:difference between the endogenous withdrawal time and bank survival timeζ−τw, is free of this
35:1295:79231:22:22:71:539:236:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:issue. Given high-frequency depositor transaction data,τrcan be measured as the time between
35:1296:79323:22:20:71:539:214:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:when withdrawals begin and when the bank fails, or until redeposits begin for a surviving bank. In
35:1297:79421:20:11:72:539:194:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:models (e.g. Grossman and Stiglitz,1980). We thank an anonymous referee for pointing out the similarity between
35:1298:79532:11:7:72:396:183:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:“bank failure” in our model and “price” in a noisy REE model as public signals.
35:1299:79611:7:15:80:539:176:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:35One real world example of this point involves the subprime mortgage crisis. On May 17, 2007 Fed Chairman
35:1300:79717:15:11:72:540:161:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:Bernanke indicated in a speech about the subprime mortgage market that looser lending standards were pervasive
35:1301:79827:11:11:72:540:150:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:especially in loans originated in 2006 (Bernanke,2007).  The speech took place at a time when low teaser rates
35:1302:79937:11:11:72:540:139:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:on many adjustable-rate mortgages were set to expire, suggesting that the rise in defaults was just the tip of an
35:1303:80050:11:11:72:540:128:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:iceberg. Subsequently, asset-backed commercial paper (ABCP) outstanding dropped from $1.3 trillion in July 2007
35:1304:80161:11:11:72:540:117:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:to $833 billion in December 2007 (Acharya, Schnabl, and Suarez,2013). One interpretation within our model of this
35:1305:80274:11:11:72:540:106:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:speech is that it signaled a relatively short awareness window, and there was not much to learn from the survival
35:1306:80387:11:11:72:540:95:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:of ABCP conduits up to that point in time. Suppose that instead that looser lending standards were pervasive in
35:1307:80498:11:10:72:540:84:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:loans originated since 2003. Having observed that the ABCP market kept growing despite this fact, investors would
35:1308:80611:10:0:72:458:74:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:perceive a high probability of the system being liquid and conclude that a run might not occur.

36:1326:80841:0:116:319:333:673:5:g_d0_f45:5:g_d0_f36:Τr*HΓL
36:1327:80847:116:14:72:540:557:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Panels (a) and (b) show the equilibrium remaining survival timeτras a function of the rumor spreading
36:1328:80948:14:13:72:540:543:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:rateβand the length of the recovery valueγ. Parameters arer= 0.09,β= 1,θ= 1.03,η= 2,p= 0.8,
36:1329:81039:13:33:72:285:530:10:g_d0_f14:10:g_d0_f4:δ= 0.12,c= 10−6,κL= 0.65,α= 0.7,γ= 0.75.
36:1330:81079:33:22:71:539:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:our model, the higher the rumor spreading speedβ, the faster the (illiquid) bank fails, the smaller
36:1331:81178:22:22:71:540:475:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the remaining survival time. The effect of bankruptcy recoveryγon the remaining survival time
36:1332:81271:22:22:71:539:453:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:τris also negative: a lower recoveryγprompts depositors to withdraw earlier, leading to a longer
36:1333:81367:22:22:71:500:431:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:remaining survival timeτr=ζ−τw. Figure5 shows these two comparative static results.
36:1334:81450:22:22:88:539:409:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Third, our model has testable implications regarding the probability of bank runs. Proposition
36:1335:81544:22:22:71:539:387:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:6 characterizes different parameter regions in which a bank run can constitute an equilibrium. By
36:1336:81641:22:22:71:539:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:assigning a probability measure on the parameter space,36one can relate model parameters to the
36:1337:81736:22:21:71:539:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:likelihood of bank runs, which has a straightforward empirical counterpart. Consider, for example,
36:1338:81834:21:22:71:540:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the rumor spreading speed.  One can show that all else equal, a largerβmakes the condition
36:1339:81924:22:22:71:540:300:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:G(τur)≥0easier to satisfy; thus Proposition6 implies that bank runs are more likely. In the
36:1340:82015:22:22:71:539:278:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:working paper version of this article, which is listed as NBER Working Paper 18513, we also show
36:1341:82111:22:22:71:539:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that the lower the information acquisition costα, the more likely is the bank run equilibrium. These
36:1342:82211:22:22:71:539:234:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are testable predictions given proxies for the spreading speed or the cost of information. Approaches
36:1343:82312:22:22:71:539:212:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for their measurement using social media and press coverage have been recently developed in the
36:1344:82407:22:22:71:277:190:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:asset pricing literature (e.g.Manela,2014).
36:1345:82450:22:22:88:539:168:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Finally, if our model withstands the above tests, one could use our structural framework to
36:1346:82541:22:22:71:539:146:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:estimate key model parameters.  For example, using the moment condition (17) of remaining
36:1347:82630:22:22:71:539:124:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:survival timeτr, one could estimate the expected deposit recovery rateγgiven bankruptcy as
36:1348:82720:22:16:71:327:102:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:perceived by depositors, a highly interesting quantity.
36:1349:82775:16:14:80:539:86:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:36In those parameter regions where multiple equilibria are possible, one need some exogenous sunspots with certain
36:1350:82889:14:0:72:258:72:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:likelihood to predict the equilibrium outcome.
37:1351:82937:0:33:72:289:709:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:6  Extensions and Discussions
37:1352:82966:33:22:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We study two extensions of our model with quadratic information acquisition cost. In Section6.1
37:1353:83061:22:22:72:540:654:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:we introduce fundamentally insolvent banks, so that it is alsosociallyefficient for individual agents
37:1354:83162:22:22:72:539:632:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to acquire information and run on insolvent banks. Section6.2 considers a two-bank economy where
37:1355:83258:22:22:71:539:610:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:competition amplifies the individual agent’s socially wasteful information production. Finally we
37:1356:83355:22:38:71:296:588:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:provide discussion on several theoretical issues.
37:1357:83404:38:29:71:296:550:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:6.1  Insolvent Banks and Stress Tests
37:1358:83441:29:29:71:381:521:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:6.1.1  Solvency information versus liquidity information
37:1359:83497:29:22:71:539:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Suppose that the bank might becomeinsolventat the timet0, which randomly fails (rather than
37:1360:83588:22:21:71:539:470:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:matures) with intensityξ > rand recovers nothing. Of course the bank can also be solvent, and if
37:1361:83684:21:22:71:347:449:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:so it can be either liquid or illiquid as we modeled before.
37:1362:83744:22:22:88:539:427:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:When agenttihears the rumor, the possibility of insolvency motivates him to spend a fixed
37:1363:83833:22:22:71:539:405:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:amount of efforte>0to obtain a signal1s∈{0,1}; for simplicity, this signal1sperfectly reveals
37:1364:83926:22:22:72:540:383:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:whether the bank is solvent or not. We focus on situations where the agent acquires this solvency
37:1365:84023:22:22:72:540:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:signal1s(which is optimal if the default intensityξis sufficiently high). Hence after hearing the
37:1366:84120:22:22:72:540:339:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rumor, all agents will figure out the bank’s insolvency and run on the insolvent bank immediately.
37:1367:84218:22:22:88:539:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The information regarding bank solvency is both socially and individually valuable. In contrast,
37:1368:84314:22:22:72:540:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the information regarding bank liquidity is individually valuable but socially destructive when
37:1369:84409:22:22:72:540:273:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents realize that runs on the illiquid bank become a concern. We aim to capture the fact that
37:1370:84504:22:22:72:540:251:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank solvency information and liquidity information are naturally linked when individual agents
37:1371:84599:22:22:72:165:229:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are acquiring them.
37:1372:84618:22:22:88:539:207:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We assume that a by-product of the agent’s private learning about bank solvency, i.e., collecting
37:1373:84715:22:21:72:540:185:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the solvency signal1s, is that he also learns something about the liquidity of the bank. To model
37:1374:84812:21:22:72:540:164:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:this, we assume that given the efforteof acquiring1s, if the bank turns out to be solvent, then the
37:1375:84911:22:22:72:539:142:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:baseline qualityqof the bank’s liquidity signaly—which is the signal we modeled in Section 4.1—is
37:1376:85008:22:18:71:540:120:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:juste. As a result, the agent’s additional liquidity information precision choice isq≥ewith cost
37:1377:85104:18:8:73:78:102:8:g_d0_f18:8:g_d0_f18:α
37:1378:85105:8:0:73:113:94:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f16:2(q−e)
37:1379:85111:0:27:113:539:103:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f4:2. The interpretation is that the process of collecting insolvency information inevitably
37:1380:85200:27:0:72:540:76:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:teaches the agent something about bank liquidity. The more effort that the agent spends in figuring
38:1381:85301:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:out whether the bank is insolvent, the more he knows about the bank’s liquidity. Our modeling
38:1382:85394:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that the effort of collecting insolvency information (i.e.,e) becomes the baseline quality of liquidity
38:1383:85497:22:37:72:314:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:information captures this idea in the simplest way.
38:1384:85548:37:29:72:285:628:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:6.1.2  Policy Implication: Stress Tests
38:1385:85587:29:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The above setting has important implications for stress tests in revealing the fundamentally prob-
38:1386:85685:22:22:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:lematic banks. Byproviding insolvency information alone, the government can use stress tests to
38:1387:85780:22:22:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:reduceeto eliminate runs on solvent-but-illiquid banks. According to our model, if a great effort is
38:1388:85880:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:required to learn about whether the bank is insolvent (say institutions like Lehman), i.e., a higher
38:1389:85980:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:e, then each agent will be automatically endowed with significant information about the liquidity
38:1390:86077:22:22:72:540:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of solvent banks (say institutions like Citibank with weak liquidity condition). As a result, runs on
38:1391:86178:22:22:72:519:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:solvent banks may start, which pushes each agent to acquire even more liquidity information.
38:1392:86270:22:22:88:540:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Stress tests provide transparency on potentially insolvent banks (Bernanke,2009), and therefore
38:1393:86365:22:22:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:reducee. Government, by providing higher quality information about banks’ insolvency, can crowd
38:1394:86460:22:22:72:540:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:out private acquisition of insolvency information. Because public information can be better targeted
38:1395:86560:22:22:72:540:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:at insolvency alone, while the process of private acquisition of solvency information inevitably
38:1396:86656:22:22:72:540:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:reveals liquidity information, public provision of solvency information helps all agents know that
38:1397:86754:22:21:72:540:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:other agents do not have superior information regarding banks liquidity situation. Therefore, our
38:1398:86851:21:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:model suggests that the public provision of insolvency information indirectly reduces the socially
38:1399:86949:22:22:72:540:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:wasteful information acquisition regarding liquidity, and therefore make runs on illiquid banks less
38:1400:87049:22:22:72:540:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:likely. Figure 6 plots the equilibrium signal precision when we varyewhich measures the extent of
38:1401:87146:22:22:72:266:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:public provision of solvency information.
38:1402:87187:22:22:88:539:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This view is consistent with the Federal Reserve Board’s recent break from the traditional
38:1403:87277:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:supervisory view of opaqueness in favor of more public disclosure to restore the confidence of
38:1404:87371:22:22:72:540:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:investors.  However, our rationale is different than the one described byBernanke(2010) who
38:1405:87462:22:22:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:argues that transparency allows for scrutiny by outside analysts, which enhances the credibility
38:1406:87558:22:22:72:540:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of the tests. Instead, we argue that by providing more information, the government crowds out
38:1407:87651:22:22:72:540:116:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the information collection effort by individuals about the solvency of the banks, and the perfect
38:1408:87748:22:16:72:539:94:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:revelation of insolvent bank clarifies the channel that we are emphasizing.37Since liquidity and
38:1409:87844:16:0:80:539:78:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:37Releasing better solvency information helps illiquid banks, but in our model it is not through a higher average
39:1410:87959:0:112:154:456:710:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Figure 6: The effect of public provision of solvency information

39:1429:88123:106:13:72:540:582:10:g_d0_f4:10:g_d0_f4:Bank run equilibrium with endogenous information acquisition when we vary the individual solvency infor-

39:1432:88404:33:22:72:540:522:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:solvency are tightly linked, this government policy has the useful by-product of reducing information
39:1433:88505:22:37:72:519:500:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:collection about bank liquidity and therefore reducing the incidence of runs on illiquid banks.
39:1434:88600:37:29:72:241:463:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:6.2  Multiple Solvent Banks
39:1435:88627:29:22:72:540:434:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We now investigate the model with competing solvent banks.  Instead of holding cash, a bank
39:1436:88718:22:22:72:540:412:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:run in this setting involves the transfer of deposited funds from one illiquid bank to another more
39:1437:88817:22:22:72:540:390:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:liquid one. Information is privately more valuable in this setup since the outside option is a nearly
39:1438:88918:22:22:72:540:368:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:identical bank rather then holding cash.  Here, the two banks’ difference might be minuscule,
39:1439:89011:22:22:72:540:346:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and transfers between the two institutions only involve social losses (transaction fees and bank
39:1440:89107:22:22:72:540:324:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:failure). Apparently, if only one of the multiple competing banks could be potentially illiquid, then
39:1441:89208:22:22:72:540:302:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:redepositing back to the surviving bank becomes off-equilibrium, as it is optimal to stay inside the
39:1442:89308:22:22:72:540:280:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:liquid competing bank. This might be the underlying reason for the finding of Iyer and Puri (2012)
39:1443:89406:22:22:72:443:258:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that only 10% of running depositors’ bank balances return to pre-crisis levels.
39:1444:89485:22:22:88:539:236:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f14:Suppose there are two banks, ex-ante identical except half the population deposits in bankA
39:1445:89576:22:22:72:539:214:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and half deposits in bankB. Both banks promise the same rate of returnr. However, transferring
39:1446:89670:22:21:72:539:192:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:funds between banks requires a transaction costc. A liquidity event occurs at a random timet0,
39:1447:89764:21:22:72:540:171:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and a rumor starts that exactly one of the banks is illiquid (withκL) while the other is liquid (with
39:1448:89865:22:21:72:540:149:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:κH). The prior probability that each bank is illiquid isp= 0.5since they are ex-ante identical. The
39:1449:89964:21:11:72:539:128:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:bank quality once the stress test isolates those insolvent ones. When the planner variese, agents can always perfectly
39:1450:90082:11:11:72:540:117:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:spot insolvent banks, therefore the channel of insolvency information is shut down. Rather, the channel is through
39:1451:90196:11:11:72:540:106:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:the strategic interaction of individual agents, as now everybody knows that everybody will wait to see the stress test
39:1452:90314:11:11:72:540:95:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:instead of scrambling to search the insolvent banks. As a result, everybody will have less precise information on
39:1453:90427:11:0:72:304:84:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:which solvent bank is less liquid and susceptible to a run.
40:1454:90488:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:learning process in the two bank set-up is simpler, because the passage of time without a failure
40:1455:90585:22:22:72:380:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:teaches agents nothing about the relative viability of their bank.
40:1456:90651:22:22:88:539:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Agents can acquire a costly signal ̃y∈ {yL,yM,yH}about their bank with probability distri-
40:1457:90741:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bution as before. Agents who receive theyHsignal know their bank is liquid and therefore never
40:1458:90835:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdraw; agents who receive theyMsignal gain no useful information and staying in their original
40:1459:90932:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank is optimal; and agents withyLsignals run on their bank immediately.38Proposition 7in the
40:1460:91025:22:22:72:434:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:AppendixA.10characterizes the equilibrium in this setting with two banks.
40:1461:91098:22:22:88:539:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In this setting, information acquisition to figure out the relative liquidity position of two solvent
40:1462:91199:22:22:71:539:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:banks is socially undesirable, as it shortens the survival time of the illiquid bank by inducing more
40:1463:91300:22:22:71:539:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents to realize that one bank strictly dominates the other. Thus it is socially beneficial to blur the
40:1464:91404:22:22:71:539:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:differences between competing solvent banks. Consider the Capital Purchase Program commonly
40:1465:91495:22:22:71:539:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:known as the bailout of the nine largest U.S. financial institutions on October 13, 2008. When
40:1466:91589:22:21:71:539:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:presenting the program to the CEOs of the 9 banks, Secretary of Treasury Henry M. Paulson was
40:1467:91682:21:22:71:539:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:concerned the strongest banks (e.g.  JPMorgan) would not participate.  To make sure they do,
40:1468:91774:22:22:71:539:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:government officials suggested that if a bank refused the funds, its regulator would later force it to
40:1469:91876:22:22:71:539:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:raise capital anyway and under worse terms.39The government was in fact injecting noise about
40:1470:91969:22:22:71:539:358:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the liquidity of competing solvent banks into the economy. By pooling banks together the incentive
40:1471:92067:22:38:71:539:336:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to transfer funds between them was kept low enough so that none of the nine banks suffered a run.
40:1472:92164:38:29:71:236:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:6.3  Other Theoretic Issues
40:1473:92191:29:37:71:450:269:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In this section we tie some theoretic loose ends and provide further discussions.
40:1474:92272:37:29:71:426:232:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:6.3.1  Minimum threshold liquidity capacityκto eliminate runs
40:1475:92333:29:22:71:539:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The dynamic rumor-based run equilibrium derived in our setting has a qualitatively different nature
40:1476:92432:22:17:71:539:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:relative to the one in the static setting (e.g.,Diamond and Dybvig(1983),Goldstein and Pauzner
40:1477:92526:17:14:80:539:164:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:38From the perspective ofyLagents, the value of a dollar in their bank falls and the value of a dollar in the
40:1478:92635:14:13:72:539:150:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f23:competing bank increases to a risklessδδ−r; as long as the transaction costcis small enough so thatVI(0|yM)<
40:1479:92743:13:11:72:539:137:9:g_d0_f24:9:g_d0_f8:(1−c)V−I(0|yH) = (1−c)δδ−r, immediate withdraw is optimal. Here, information is (privately) more valuable in
40:1480:92851:11:7:72:420:126:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:this setup since the outside option is a nearly identical bank rather then holding cash.
40:1481:92939:7:15:80:539:119:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:39“I was concerned about Jamie Dimon, because JPMorgan appeared to be in the best shape of the group, and I
40:1482:93046:15:11:72:540:104:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:wanted to be sure he would accept the capital.” “Look, we’re making you an offer,” I said, jumping in. “If you don’t
40:1483:93162:11:11:72:540:93:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:take it and sometime later your regulator tells you that you are undercapitalized and you have to raise private-sector
40:1484:93280:11:0:72:534:82:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:capital but you are unable to do so, you may not like the terms if you have to come back to me.” -Paulson(2010)
41:1485:93393:0:22:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(2005)). Unlike the typical static setting where runs occur if bank reserves are below all potential
41:1486:93493:22:22:72:540:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdrawals, our rich dynamic setting gives a non-trivial minimum reserve threshold that eliminates
41:1487:93592:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the run equilibrium. In other words, even for the illiquid bank, the minimum reserve requirement
41:1488:93688:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to fence off bank runs,κL, is below1which is the level that is sufficient to cover all potential
41:1489:93784:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdrawals.  As fully analyzed in the working paper version NBER Working Paper 18513 and
41:1490:93873:22:22:72:540:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:explained briefly in AppendixB.1, this result is rooted in the uncertainty over the timing of liquidity
41:1491:93976:22:22:72:486:577:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:event and other depositors’ withdrawal timings in our asynchronous awareness setting.
41:1492:94061:22:22:88:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Following the same logic, there exists a minimum reserve threshold forκH, so that rumor-based
41:1493:94154:22:22:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bank runs never occur for the liquid bank as long asκHis above this threshold. This result justifies
41:1494:94254:22:22:72:540:511:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the assumption that staying in the bank is optimal given ayHsignal (and hence the bank is liquid),
41:1495:94352:22:37:72:488:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:which we have taken as given in Section4.1. For detailed argument, see AppendixB.1.
41:1496:94435:37:29:72:289:452:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:6.3.2  What about uninformed agents?
41:1497:94471:29:22:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Uninformed agents play no role in our analysis of rumor-based bank runs. So far, we have assumed
41:1498:94567:22:22:72:540:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that uninformed agents remain fully deposited before they hear the rumor.  We now provide a
41:1499:94658:22:22:72:540:379:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:justification for the optimality of this strategy. Uninformed learning is more complicated because,
41:1500:94757:22:22:72:540:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in addition to the failure hazard rate, they keep updating the rumor arrival rate, i.e. the probability
41:1501:94860:22:21:72:540:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of hearing the rumor in the next instant given no bank failure and no rumor. Nevertheless, because
41:1502:94958:21:22:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:it does not matter much whether an agent hears the rumor inside or outside the bank (up to small
41:1503:95054:22:22:72:490:292:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:transaction costs), the rumor arrival rate plays a minor role in the withdrawal decision.
41:1504:95143:22:22:88:539:270:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The failure hazard rate from the perspective of uninformed agents, on the other hand, is im-
41:1505:95235:22:22:72:540:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:portant even when transaction costs vanish. Importantly, the failure hazard rate converges to zero
41:1506:95333:22:22:72:540:226:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ast→ ∞; a formal analysis is available upon request. Intuitively, as time passes and uninformed
41:1507:95428:22:22:72:540:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents observe no failure and no rumor, they will attach a higher and higher probability to the
41:1508:95523:22:22:72:539:182:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:event that ̃t0already happened (and they missed the rumor), but the bank is liquid so no failure
41:1509:95619:22:22:72:540:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:occurs. Similar to the analysis for informed agents in (11), an uninformed agent will stay inside
41:1510:95716:22:39:72:347:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the bank from timetgoing forward if the following holds:
41:1511:95772:39:0:208:539:99:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:hU(s) (1−γ) (1−c)≤rUI(s)fors≥t,(22)
42:1512:95809:0:22:72:539:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:wherehU(s)andUI(s)are the failure hazard rate and the value of an inside dollar perceived
42:1513:95898:22:22:72:539:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:by uninformed agents.  Since whent→ ∞the failure hazard rate decreases to zero, while the
42:1514:95987:22:22:72:540:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:right hand sideUI(s)> pγ(1−c) + (1−p)(1−c)δδ−r,40condition (22) must hold for anytsuch that
42:1515:96078:22:22:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f4:0≤tf≤t <∞, for some finitetf. In fact, for the parameters chosen to illustrate our results, the
42:1516:96173:22:22:72:540:621:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:maximum hazard rate is sufficiently low thattf= 0, i.e. it is always optimal for uninformed agents
42:1517:96271:22:46:72:195:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to remain fully deposited.
42:1518:96297:46:32:72:173:553:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:7  Conclusion
42:1519:96310:32:22:72:540:521:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We study above new dimensions of bank runs, previously unexplored, by focusing on information
42:1520:96403:22:22:72:540:499:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:acquisition in rumor-based runs.  Our model incorporates uncertainty and information acquisi-
42:1521:96496:22:22:72:540:477:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tion about bank liquidity into the asynchronous awareness framework ofAbreu and Brunnermeier
42:1522:96588:22:22:72:540:455:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(2003). Information acquisition about liquidity exposes otherwise safe banks to destructive runs
42:1523:96684:22:22:72:540:433:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:with endogenous waiting through a “fear-of-bad-signal-agents” effect: agents unsure about bank
42:1524:96778:22:22:72:540:411:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:liquidity worry that agents who receive worse signals withdraw before them, which increases their
42:1525:96875:22:22:72:540:389:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:own incentives to run. Even in the situation where runs never occur without information acqui-
42:1526:96969:22:22:72:540:367:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:sition, this effect of information acquisition results in a unique and interior bank run equilibrium
42:1527:97069:22:22:72:262:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:with an endogenous bank survival time.
42:1528:97107:22:21:88:539:323:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We use our model to analyze the role that government information policy can play in bank run
42:1529:97199:21:22:72:540:302:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:prevention, when solvency is uncertain, and in a multiple bank setting. Empirically, our model
42:1530:97293:22:22:72:540:280:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:sheds new light on both traditional bank runs and debt runs more broadly.  Our model makes
42:1531:97383:22:22:72:540:258:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:new predictions linking the likelihood of a run to the spreading rate of the rumor, the cost of
42:1532:97478:22:22:72:540:236:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:acquiring information, and the recovery value in case of bankruptcy. It also generates the unique
42:1533:97575:22:22:72:540:214:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:prediction that for banks that survive a run, we should observe agents withdraw at the same time
42:1534:97671:22:22:72:540:192:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:earlier informed agents redeposit. Our model is flexible and rich enough for structural estimation
42:1535:97769:22:22:72:540:170:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:or calibration of its parameters given detailed withdrawals data, which can result in meaningful
42:1536:97865:22:22:72:540:148:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:policy implications. In the Appendix, we discuss the possibility of depositors choosing the optimal
42:1537:97964:22:16:72:540:126:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:time to acquire signals (SectionB.2), and the possibility of endogenizing the rumor spreading speed
42:1538:98063:16:15:80:539:110:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:40The lower bound for the valueUI(s)is achieved under the simple strategy of never withdrawing from the bank,
42:1539:98172:15:11:72:540:95:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:and assuming that the illiquid bank fails immediately. This is a lower bound because i) the illiquid bank survives
42:1540:98286:11:11:72:540:84:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:for a while; and ii) at any later time, the posterior probability of an illiquid bank conditional on no failure is weakly
42:1541:98407:11:0:72:462:73:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:lower than their priorp(similar to the effect in (21); the formal proof is available upon request).
43:1542:98508:0:22:72:138:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(Section B.3).
43:1543:98522:22:22:88:539:687:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:More broadly, the dynamic bank run model we provide above can shed new light on other
43:1544:98607:22:56:72:524:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:economic settings such as arbitrageur behavior, currency attacks, and R&D investment games.

52:2346:118148:46:33:72:370:384:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:B  Additional Results and Extensions6.3
52:2347:118187:33:29:72:465:351:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B.1  Minimum Liquidity Capacity Threshold that Eliminate Runs
52:2348:118248:29:15:72:539:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The threshold liquidity capacityκLthat eliminates bank runs on the illiquid bank can be found
52:2349:118341:15:0:72:224:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f14:numerically as theκLso thatG
52:2350:118369:0:11:226:232:318:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:(
52:2351:118370:11:0:232:275:307:11:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f18:τlr(q) ;κL
52:2352:118380:0:11:276:282:318:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:)
52:2353:118381:11:19:285:539:307:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f4:= 0in Proposition5 with binary information choices,
52:2354:118432:19:0:72:94:288:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f14:orG
52:2355:118435:0:11:95:101:299:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:(
52:2356:118436:11:0:101:154:288:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f16:τlr(q∗|ζ∗=η)
52:2357:118448:0:11:154:160:299:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:)
52:2358:118449:11:15:163:539:288:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f4:= 0in Proposition6 with convex acquisition costs. In the baseline parameters
52:2359:118525:15:13:71:344:273:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in Figure4, the threshold liquidity capacityκLis 0.6537.
52:2360:118581:13:14:88:539:260:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In general, due to the asynchronous nature of our rumor-based setting, even without information
52:2361:118676:14:13:71:539:246:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:acquisition, immediate withdrawal after hearing the rumor might not be an equilibrium. Similar to
52:2362:118773:13:14:71:540:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the insight ofAbreu and Brunnermeier(2003), this is because the depositor knows that the bank
52:2363:118866:14:14:71:539:219:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:survives for a while, a feature absent in any static bank run setting. Thus, eliminating dynamic
52:2364:118962:14:13:71:533:205:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rumor-based runs requires less liquidity reserve than the one suggested by the static perspective.
52:2365:119060:13:14:88:540:192:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Here is an outline on how to determine the threshold thresholdκHso that there never exist runs
52:2366:119154:14:13:71:539:178:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:on the liquid bank. Our information structure in Figure2 implies that the agent withyHknows the
52:2367:119249:13:14:71:538:165:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f18:bank is liquid for sure. More importantly, the agent knows that he is among theqfraction ofyH
52:2368:119342:14:13:71:540:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents, and there are1−qfraction of informed agents with medium signalsyM. We are interested
52:2369:119434:13:14:71:540:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in the equilibrium behavior ofyHagents who endogenously wait a while to withdraw, by holding
52:2370:119526:14:13:71:540:124:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the belief that1−qfraction ofyMagents withdraw immediately upon hearing the rumor. Thus,
52:2371:119614:13:17:71:539:111:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:yHagents face a tradeoff similar to (11). This harshest belief regardingyMagents allows us to
52:2372:119707:17:7:80:388:94:6:g_d0_f7:5:g_d0_f27:41In this two-bank setting we no longer impose the restriction ofq≤κL
52:2373:119776:7:8:370:540:87:6:g_d0_f21:9:g_d0_f8:1−e−βηas in condition (16), because now
52:2374:119815:8:0:72:373:79:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:onlyyLagents are withdrawing to potentially take down the illiquid bank.
53:2375:119889:0:14:72:539:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:determine the upper bound of theκHthreshold that rules out runs byyHagents. Interestingly, this
53:2376:119984:14:14:72:539:695:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f18:is in the same nature as the equilibrium for the illiquid bank studied in the main model, whereyL
53:2377:120081:14:13:72:540:681:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents withdraw immediately whileyMagents wait for a while; and hence the same algorithm that
53:2378:120174:13:14:72:539:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:pins down thresholdκLapplies.42Under our baseline parameters given in Figure4, the threshold
53:2379:120266:14:37:72:353:654:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f4:κHrequired to eliminate runs on the liquid bank is 0.8241.
53:2380:120324:37:29:72:401:617:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B.2  Optimal Time to Acquire the Additional Signal(s)
53:2381:120377:29:14:72:540:588:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We have so far assumed agents acquire the additional signalyimmediately upon hearing the
53:2382:120465:14:14:72:540:574:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rumor. Although early information allows for a superior action, there is an option value derived
53:2383:120561:14:13:72:540:560:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:from waiting to acquire the signal later: the agent learns from the passage of time that the bank is
53:2384:120661:13:14:72:539:547:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:more likely to be liquid, and the bank might fail (thus making the additional signal unnecessary).
53:2385:120759:14:13:88:539:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The following Proposition provides a sufficient condition for the optimality of acquiring infor-

53:2387:120952:14:31:72:315:506:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:relative to the net benefit of delaying this expense.

53:2433:122061:15:11:72:540:115:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:wish to wait longer. Once the resulting survival timeζexceeds the awareness windowη, the similar logic as in Lemma
53:2434:122175:11:11:72:539:104:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f23:2 and Proposition 4implies thatyHagents will not run in equilibrium. Here, the implicit assumption is that1−q
53:2435:122284:11:0:71:320:93:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:measure ofyMagents are not enough to take down the bank.

54:2456:122700:0:9:329:334:586:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:(

54:2460:122749:13:15:72:539:564:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdrawing dominates acquiring it just after. Using the fact thatVI(τw|yM) = (1−c)VO(τw|yM),
54:2461:122842:15:14:72:539:549:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the earlier region dominates if and only ifq(1−p(τw))(1−c)δδ−rc≥χ(q)c, which is guaranteed under
54:2462:122938:14:13:71:540:535:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:condition (29). The intuition is that since the money is inside the bank just beforeτw, an agent
54:2463:123034:13:14:71:539:522:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:who withdraws, acquires information, and then redeposits would waste the transaction cost, but
54:2464:123128:14:14:71:539:508:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:gain on the proportional cost of information by delaying it until after he pays transaction cost to
54:2465:123227:14:13:71:119:494:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdraw.
54:2466:123236:13:14:88:539:481:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We could also allow agents to acquire signals more than once. But if we impose, as one should, a
54:2467:123332:14:13:71:539:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:small fixed cost of acquiring information, we get in equilibrium a finite number of such acquisitions.
54:2468:123434:13:14:71:539:454:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:After these, the population is fully described by the same three types (yL,yM,yH) as in the main
54:2469:123530:14:38:71:448:440:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:text. Thus, the bank run equilibrium structure remains qualitatively the same.
54:2470:123608:38:29:71:322:402:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:B.3  Endogenous Rumor Spreading Speed
54:2471:123645:29:13:71:539:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:One can extend our model by linking the spreading speed to the fraction already informed, which
54:2472:123740:13:14:71:540:360:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:leads the equilibrium fraction of informed agents to be anS-shaped function in the spreading time.
54:2473:123838:14:13:71:539:346:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Such a modification only makes the conditional distribution for ̃t0in (2) more complicated, but
54:2474:123933:13:14:71:232:333:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:would not affect our main results.
54:2475:123967:14:13:88:540:319:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A more ambitious/interesting extension would be to follow the spirit ofBanerjee(1993) by
54:2476:124055:13:15:71:539:306:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:allowing the spreading speed to depend on the fraction of depositors who have run on the bank, say
54:2477:124153:15:0:71:265:291:11:g_d0_f14:11:g_d0_f16:βR(t|t0, ̃κ)dtwhereR(t|t0, ̃κ) = (1−q)
54:2478:124191:0:11:267:273:302:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:(
54:2479:124192:11:0:273:334:291:11:g_d0_f16:8:g_d0_f19:1−e−β(t−τw)
54:2480:124203:0:11:335:341:302:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:)
54:2481:124204:11:0:344:360:291:11:g_d0_f16:11:g_d0_f14:+q
54:2482:124206:0:11:362:368:302:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:(
54:2483:124207:11:0:368:406:291:11:g_d0_f16:8:g_d0_f18:1−e−βt
54:2484:124213:0:11:407:413:302:10:g_d0_f17:10:g_d0_f17:)
54:2485:124214:11:15:416:539:291:11:g_d0_f15:11:g_d0_f4:×1{κL}is the cumulative
54:2486:124237:15:13:71:540:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:withdrawal shown in Figure3. As a result, the rumor spreading speed depends on not only the
54:2487:124328:13:14:71:539:263:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:underlying bank liquidity ̃κ, but also the endogenous equilibrium waiting timeτwofyMagents.
54:2488:124419:14:13:71:539:249:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Both can be viewed as amplification forces.  First, sinceyLagents immediately withdraw only
54:2489:124510:13:14:71:539:236:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:when the bank is illiquid, relative to the case of ̃κ=κHthe rumor spreads faster, giving rise
54:2490:124603:14:14:71:539:222:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of a more severe run on the illiquid bank. Second, ifyMagents wait a bit longer to withdraw,
54:2491:124695:14:13:71:539:208:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the rumor spreading speed is slower, and thus the illiquid bank will survive longer, feeding back
54:2492:124792:13:14:71:539:195:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to later withdrawal ofyMagents. Although mathematically challenging, the critical feature for
54:2493:124885:14:13:71:539:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:our analysis, that the hazard rates depend only on time elapsed since hearing the rumor, would
54:2494:124979:13:14:71:539:168:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:be preserved. As a result, with the aid of numerical methods one can analyze such settings with
54:2495:125074:14:0:71:398:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:endogenous rumors, and we leave this possibility for future research.
55:2496:125145:0:33:72:281:709:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C  Non-stationary Equilibria
55:2497:125173:33:14:72:540:676:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We consider the non-stationary part of the model here.  Ift0< η, then some early informed
55:2498:125262:14:13:72:540:662:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:agents withti< ηknows thatt0∈[0,ti], and this truncation implies strategy may beti-dependent.
55:2499:125355:13:14:72:539:649:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:However, as shown inAbreu and Brunnermeier(2003), those early agents will be bunching together
55:2500:125449:14:13:71:418:635:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to eliminate the non-stationarity. We modify their results to our setting.
55:2501:125523:13:14:88:540:622:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Focus on the bank being illiquid. To be precise, followAbreu and Brunnermeier(2003) in our
55:2502:125613:14:13:71:540:608:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:model the agents who hears the rumor beforeζ−τw=τrwill behave as if the agent who hears the
55:2503:125704:13:14:71:539:595:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rumor exactly atτr. The strategy of the agent who hears rumor atτris that, independent of signal
55:2504:125800:14:14:71:539:581:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(yLoryM) he will withdraw atτr+τw=ζ. Moreover, for agents who hear rumor atti∈[τr,ζ],
55:2505:125885:14:13:71:540:567:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:they take the following strategy. If they receiveyLsignal then he will withdraw atζ, while if they
55:2506:125983:13:14:71:539:554:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:getyMsignal then they withdraw atti+τw. This additional modification is because relative to
55:2507:126074:14:13:71:454:540:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Abreu and Brunnermeier(2003) agents may have different signals in our model.
